401 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Adkins


A04-1692


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


706 N.W.2d 59; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 780



November 15, 2005, Decided  
November 22, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court File No. K5034673.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree burglary in the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota. He appealed, asserting the district court erred by denying his motion to suppress identification evidence. He also asserted that the district court erroneously sentenced him as a career offender under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 4 (2004) in violation of his right to a jury determination of aggravating sentencing factors.


OVERVIEW: The record showed that a 15-year-old resident of the burglarized home came face to face with defendant. Police stopped defendant on foot not far from the residence within 25 minutes. The aforementioned teenager then identified defendant while looking out the window of a squad car. The appellate court rejected defendant's argument that the district court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress the show-up identification. Although the procedure utilized was unnecessarily suggestive, under the totality of the circumstances, the identification had adequate independent origin and was reliable. However, as to defendant's sentencing, Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 4 (2004) (the career-offender statute) authorized an upward departure based on a judicial determination at the time of sentencing about the nature of the crime for which sentence was being imposed. The appellate court held that § 609.1095, subd. 4 was unconstitutional to the extent that it authorized a judicial finding that a pattern of criminal conduct existed. Because the statute was unconstitutional as applied to defendant's sentence, a reversal of his sentence was in order.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but his sentence was reversed, and the matter was remanded for resentencing consistent with the appellate court's opinion.

State v. Shattuck


C6-03-362


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA

403 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Brink v. Smith Cos. Constr., Inc.


A05-5


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


703 N.W.2d 871; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 762



September 27, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Brink v. Smith Cos. Constr., Inc., 2005 Minn. LEXIS 828 (Minn., Dec. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court File No. C6-03-1331.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a general contractor, challenged a grant of summary judgment by the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, to respondents, several subcontractors, which dismissed the general contractor's third-party claims for contribution and indemnity. The general contractor had brought its third-party claims after it was sued for breach of warranty under Minn. Stat. § 327A.02 (2002).


OVERVIEW: Because the general contractor's claims were for contribution and indemnity, the actions were subject to both the two-year statute of limitations and the 10 to 12 year statute of repose, Minn. Stat. § 541.051, subd. 1(a), served to bar the claims. The general contractor argued that because § 541.051, subd. 1(a) as applied foreclosed its third-party claims before they accrued, that same violated its due-process rights under the state and federal constitutions and its right to a remedy under the Minnesota Constitution. The appellate court held that when a party was sued for breach of statutory warranty and was completely foreclosed from asserting third-party claims for contribution and indemnity by the statute of repose under Minn. Stat. § 541.051, subd. 1(a) (2002), same violated that party's due-process rights under the federal and state constitutions and its right to a remedy under the Minnesota Constitution. Thus, the district court committed reversible error in granting summary judgment fort the subcontractors. The appellate court emphasized that § 541.051, subd. 1(a), was unconstitutional only as applied to the general contractor's third-party contribution and indemnity claims.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

 

404 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bren


A05-812


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


704 N.W.2d 170; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 754



September 20, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Bren, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 788 (Minn., Dec. 13, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court File No. 03038189.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the president of a bankrupt home construction company, was charged with counts of unlawful failure to use proceeds paid for the improvement to real estate, theft by swindle, theft by false representation, and fraud in obtaining credit. The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, granted defendant's motion to dismiss eight of the counts on grounds that Minn. Stat. § 514.02 (2000) was unconstitutional. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State argued that Minn. Stat. § 514.02 (2000) was constitutional because it did not imprison for the nonpayment of a debt, but criminalized the violation of a statutorily created trust-like relationship between a contractor and a homeowner. The appellate court agreed, finding that it was a contractor's knowing violation of the "trust character" of the payments entrusted to him by the homeowner, rather than any failure to pay a debt to a subcontractor, that made a contractor criminally liable under the statute. The statute punished a contractor's misapplication of payments received from a homeowner, as opposed to punishing the failure to pay a debt owed to subcontractors. Contrary to defendant's contention, the language in Minn. Stat. § 514.02, subd. 1(a) (2000) negating fiduciary liability necessarily applied only to the limited civil cause of action created by the statute in subd. 1(a). The appellate court concluded that the trial court erred in determining that the statute violated the constitutional prohibition against imprisonment for debt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the trial court to reinstate the eight counts of the complaint that were dismissed by the trial court.

 

405 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reinke


A04-2219


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


702 N.W.2d 308; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 737



August 23, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chippewa County District Court. File No. T0-04-685.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Chippewa County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted her of violating Big Bend Township, Minn., Zoning Ordinance Relating to Dogs § 1.04(B).


OVERVIEW: Section 1.04(B) was passed approximately one and one-half years after defendant bought her residence. The ordinance prohibited three or more dogs on premises owned by any individual residing in the township's high density population area. Defendant was found guilty of violating the ordinance. On appeal, the court found that defendant failed to meet her burden of proving that it was not even debatable that regulating the number of dogs per residence had a substantial relationship to controlling the problems of dog noise, temperament, and odor as they affected the public health, safety, and welfare. Defendant had not overcome the ordinance's presumption of constitutionality. Further, because defendant's conviction pertained to keeping three or more dogs on her residential premises after the ordinance was passed, it did not violate the prohibition against ex post facto laws. Finally, because defendant's dog-breeding business, was not in lawful use at the time of the enactment of the ordinance limiting the number of dogs per residential premises, the exception for preexisting nonconforming uses did not permit her continued violation of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

406 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Sweet v. Comm'r of Human Servs.


A04-2274


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


702 N.W.2d 314; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 735; 23 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 599



August 23, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Sweet v. Comm'r of Human Servs., 2005 Minn. LEXIS 721 (Minn., Nov. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Department of Human Services.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, a proposed counselor (counselor), sought review of the decision of respondent, the Commissioner of the Minnesota Department of Human Services (commissioner), which denied the counselor's request to set aside his disqualification from working as a counselor.


OVERVIEW: The counselor challenged the commissioner's decision denying the counselor's request to set aside his disqualification from working as a counselor in a state-licensed program because of his criminal record, including convictions of first-degree and third-degree criminal sexual conduct. The court affirmed however, stating that substantial evidence supported the commissioner's decision and that the counselor had the opportunity and exercised his right to present written evidence to the commissioner. The counselor presented no medical or psychological evidence to support his contention that he was fully rehabilitated. Further, the counselor refused to take responsibility for his actions and blamed the victim for his convictions. Application of the Mathews balancing test showed that an evidentiary hearing was not required to afford the counselor with procedural due process. Providing him with the right to submit evidence in writing was adequate to meet the requirements of due process. Consequently, the statutory language contained in Minn. Stat. § 245C.27, subd. 1(c) (2004) that an applicant was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing was not unconstitutional on its face or as applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

407 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shattuck


C6-03-362


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


704 N.W.2d 131; 2005 Minn. LEXIS 476



August 18, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, Amended by State v. Shattuck, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 581 (2005)
Appeal after remand at State v. Shattuck, 2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 626 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of Appeals. Office of Appellate Courts. LOWER COURT JUDGE: Honorable Jeanne J. Graham, Hennepin County District Court.
State v. Shattuck, 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 349 (Minn. Ct. App., Apr. 13, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Minnesota Court of Appeals, which affirmed a sentence entered in a sexual assault and kidnapping case.


OVERVIEW: An enhanced sentence was imposed under Minn. Stat. § 609.109, subd. 4(a) (2004) for a sexual assault conviction. Thereafter, defendant sought review. The court of appeals affirmed the sentence imposed. In reversing, the court determined that defendant's Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial was violated by the imposition of the enhanced sentence. The Minnesota Sentencing Guidelines were not merely advisory, pursuant to the language in Minn. Stat. § 244.09, subd. 5. Further, because Minn. Stat. § 609.109, subd. 4 (2004), and Minn. Sentencing Guidelines II.D authorized the district court to make an unconstitutional upward durational departure upon finding an aggravating factor without the aid of a jury, these provisions were facially unconstitutional. The court determined that Minn. Stat. § 609.109, subd. 4 (2004) was unconstitutional in its entirety. However, the Minnesota Sentencing Guidelines were not totally invalidated. Rather, the appropriate remedy was to sever the unconstitutional guideline from the rest of the statutory scheme, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 645.20. The court declined the State's suggestion to make the Minnesota Sentencing Guidelines advisory.


OUTCOME: The sentence was reversed, and the case was remanded to the district court for the imposition of a sentence within the presumptive range.

 

408 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hannon


A04-434


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


703 N.W.2d 498; 2005 Minn. LEXIS 485



August 18, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent civil proceeding at Hannon v. Sanner, 441 F.3d 635, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 7542 (8th Cir. Minn., 2006)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Hannon v. Sanner, 2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 746 (2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hannon v. State, 752 N.W.2d 518, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 324 (2008)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Hannon v. State, 781 N.W.2d 887, 2010 Minn. LEXIS 238 (2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hannon v. State, 2017 Minn. LEXIS 52 (Minn., Feb. 8, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Stearns County.
State v. Hannon, 636 N.W.2d 796, 2001 Minn. LEXIS 813 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Stearns County District Court (Minnesota) of first-degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the district court erred in refusing his request for a jury instruction on second-degree unintentional felony murder. The supreme court disagreed. Neither party presented evidence that created a rational basis for the jury to conclude that defendant unintentionally killed the victim during an assault. The theory of defense was that defendant did not assault and kill the victim. Defense counsel argued during closing that the shirt found shortly after the murder with defendant's DNA and the victim's blood on it was planted by the police, that officers fabricated defendant's confessions, and that defendant's conduct the night of the killing did not comport with the conduct of someone who had recently beaten his girlfriend to death. That theory was inconsistent with the requested lesser-included offense instruction, and no other evidence was presented to indicate that defendant unintentionally killed the victim during an assault.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

409 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Kahn v. Griffin


A04-1646


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


701 N.W.2d 815; 2005 Minn. LEXIS 471



August 11, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certified Question. LOWER COURT JUDGE: Hon. John Tunheim, U.S. District Court.
Kahn v. Griffin, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 18444 (D. Minn., Aug. 31, 2004).



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter was before the court on a certified question from the United States District Court for the District of Minnesota as to whether the Minnesota Constitution provides greater protections to the right to vote than the U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV such that the failure to hold prompt elections following decennial redistricting violates Minn. Const. art. I, § 2 and VII, § 1 or Minn. Stat. §§ 204B.135, subd. 1, and 204B.14, subd. 1a (2004).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff citizens filed suit, requesting that the court order the city to hold a new city council election because Minneapolis, Minn., City Charter ch. 1, § 3 and Code of Ordinances, ch, 1, § 3(F), which allowed city council members to complete their term despite redistricting, resulted in malapportioned districts and were unconstitutional. The federal court held that the city's failure to hold an immediate election did not violate the federal constitution in light of the city's burdens and costs of holding an extra election and the state's compelling interest in preserving the orderliness and integrity of the election process. The federal court certified the question of whether the Minnesota Constitution afforded greater protection and whether the failure to hold an election violated Minn. Stat. §§ 204B.135, subd. 1, and 204B.14, subd. 1a. The court held that the Minnesota Constitution did not provide greater protection because the right to vote was deemed a fundamental right under both the federal and state constitutions and plaintiffs failed to provide any principled basis for the court to depart from the concept of uniformity in following federal precedent.


OUTCOME: The court held that the failure of the city to hold elections immediately following the city's decennial redistricting of its wards did not unconstitutionally burden the right to vote; and thus did not violate the Minnesota Constitution or statutes.

 

410 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schmidt


A05-218


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


701 N.W.2d 313; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 724



August 9, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Schmidt, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 664 (Minn., Oct. 26, 2005)
Reversed by State v. Schmidt, 2006 Minn. LEXIS 208 (Minn., Apr. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Faribault County District Court. File No. KX-04-94.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with DWI, refusal, driving after revocation, and open bottle. Defendant moved to dismiss. The Faribault County District Court, Minnesota, granted the motion. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant moved to dismiss because his prior convictions and revocations used to enhance the current charges were from South Dakota, and he was not advised of his right to counsel prior to submitting to any chemical testing in South Dakota. The appellate court agreed. A motorist's South Dakota DWI convictions and license revocations, based on uncounseled chemical testing, violated the motorist's Minnesota constitutional right to assistance of counsel before deciding whether to submit to alcohol-concentration testing. The South Dakota convictions and revocations could not be used for enhancement purposes. The appellate court further concluded that an exclusionary-rule analysis was inappropriate when prior DWI convictions and license revocations were used to enhance a current charge. The State had not clearly demonstrated that the district court erred in its application of the law to the undisputed facts of this case.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

411 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hartmann


A03-1674


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


700 N.W.2d 449; 2005 Minn. LEXIS 421



July 28, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of Appeals. Office of Appellate Courts. Hon. Terrence E. Conkel, MeLeod County District Court.
State v. Hartmann, 681 N.W.2d 690, 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 715 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a couple who owned a small farm, were convicted of selling their meat products without a license under the Minnesota Consolidated Food Licensing Law in violation of Minn. Stat. § 28A.04, and unauthorized sale of custom-processed meat in violation of Minn. Stat. § 31A.10(4), in the MeLeod County District Court, Minnesota. The Minnesota Court of Appeals affirmed their convictions. The instant court granted review.


OVERVIEW: The record showed the State's secret agents performed surveillance on the couple and purchased from the couple small quantities of custom-processed ground beef, wieners, pork chops, beef liver, and bacon. Later, a compliance officer picked up an order of meat from the couple. The State then filed its complaints. At issue on appeal was the meaning of Minn. Const. art. XIII, § 7. The supreme court held that the clear and unambiguous language of Minn. Const. art. XIII, § 7 permitted any person to sell the products of his or her farm, including meat products, without obtaining a license. Thus, the couple could not be prosecuted for failure to have obtained a license to sell their meat products. However, Minn. Const. art. XIII, § 7 did not exempt a farmer from health and safety regulations that prohibited the sale of uninspected meat. Further, Minn. Stat. § 31A.15, subd. 1 (2004) only exempted a farmer from inspection regulations for custom-processed meat if the meat was used exclusively in the household of the owner; such use of custom-processed meat did not allow sale of the meat to others. Thus, the couples' convictions for selling custom-processed meat were upheld.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

412 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Palubicki


A04-1318


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


700 N.W.2d 476; 2005 Minn. LEXIS 418; 23 A.L.R.6th 835



July 28, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Palubicki v. Minnesota, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 102433 (D. Minn., Mar. 1, 2006)
Appeal after remand at State v. Palubicki, 727 N.W.2d 662, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 80 (Feb. 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hubbard County. Office of Appellate Courts. Honorable John P. Smith, Hubbard County District Court.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed and remanded for re-adjudication and sentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hubbard County District Court (Minnesota) of one count of first-degree premeditated murder and two counts of first-degree felony murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by allowing defendant's wife and her father to testify about what she heard defendant say when he came home the night the victim was murdered without first determining whether the purported communications were protected by the marital privilege. The supreme court disagreed. Circumstances surrounding the statements did not indicate that defendant intended for his wife to acquire some knowledge from his words. The record suggested that when defendant made the statements he was angry with the way things had gone at the victim's house and was indifferent to his wife's presence. He did not specifically direct his words to her, nor was there an indication that he expected his wife to be awake when he entered the house, slammed the front door, pounded down the hallway, and screamed that things had gone wrong. Because the challenged statements were not directed at or intended to convey a message to defendant's wife, they were not protected by the marital privilege, and therefore their admission was proper.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed and the case was remanded to the trial court for the re-adjudication of the convictions and sentencing.

 

413 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Estrella


A05-43


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


700 N.W.2d 496; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 702



July 12, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Estrella, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 707 (Minn., Nov. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Rice County District Court. File No.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a pretrial order of the Rice County District Court (Minnesota), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the racketeering charge against him for lack of probable cause and which denied the State's motion to add second-degree controlled substance offense charges based on defendant's alleged sale of cocaine within a "park zone" as defined in Minn. Stat. § 152.01.


OVERVIEW: With respect to the racketeering charge, the issue was whether the district court's primary finding that there was no evidence of a criminal enterprise between defendant and his parents was a legal determination. The court determined that it was an issue of fact, and that Minn. R. Crim. P. 28.04, subd. 1(1)(a) prohibited the State from appealing a pretrial dismissal if it was based solely on a factual determination dismissing a complaint for lack of probable cause. The court next examined the definition of "park zone" in Minn. Stat. § 152.01 and found that it was ambiguous in its definition of how far from the actual park boundary a "park zone" extended. The phrase "one city block" in § 152.01, subd. 12a, was undefined. The court agreed with defendant that the legislature contemplated cases where the park and its "adjoining areas" were not laid out in city blocks and therefore included the alternative measurement of 300 feet. Because the only evidence on the record showed that the trailers where the alleged drug transactions took place were not within 300 feet of the park, the court affirmed the denial of the motion to add charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

414 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Mayo Collaborative Servs. v. Comm'r of Revenue


A04-2190


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


698 N.W.2d 408; 2005 Minn. LEXIS 368



June 30, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Mayo Collaborative Servs. v. Cir of Mn, 126 S. Ct. 1334, 164 L. Ed. 2d 50, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 1164 (U.S., Feb. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tax Court. Office of Appellate Courts.
Mayo Collaborative Servs. v. Comm'r of Revenue, 2004 Minn. Tax LEXIS 52 (Minn. T.C., Sept. 21, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator medical laboratory (lab) appealed the judgment of the Tax Court, Office of Appellate Courts (Minnesota), which upheld the MinnesotaCare tax of Minn. Stat. §§ 295.50, subd. 4; 295.51, subd. 1; 295.52, subd. 7 (2000) and affirmed the decision of respondent Minnesota Commissioner of Revenue to deny the lab's claims for MinnesotaCare tax exemption (exemption) of revenues from non-Minnesota health-care providers.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner allowed the lab to deduct as exempt revenue received from Minnesota entities but disallowed deductions from non-Minnesota receipts. The tax court reasoned that the exemption was not facially discriminatory because it was not based on geography and was internally consistent and thus fairly apportioned because the tax was being assessed on a single taxpayer, the Minnesota lab, and there was no risk that any state would impose tax on the same health-care service more than once. The court affirmed the decision. The exemption was based on whether the revenue was received from a hospital, surgical center, or a health-care provider on whom liability for tax was imposed, without explicit reference to the location of that provider under Minn. Stat. § 295.53, subd. 1(a)(4)-(5). Because decisions of the United States Supreme Court suggested that the Interstate Commerce Clause did not require equal treatment when an exemption was allowed for payment by a third party of a separate in-state tax but not of a separate out-of-state tax, the court affirmed the conclusion that the MinnesotaCare statute was not facially discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court.

 

415 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rinehart


A04-1671


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 680



June 21, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Stay granted by State v. Rinehart, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 603 (2005)
Review denied by State v. Rinehart, 2006 Minn. LEXIS 740 (Minn., Oct. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. William R. Howard, Judge. District Court File No. 04035149.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to one count of controlled substance crime in the fifth-degree. The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, sentenced defendant to an enhanced term of 36 months imprisonment based on the finding that the gun was in close proximity to the drugs and could have been used in furtherance of a drug transaction. Defendant appealed her sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted to possession of Oxycontin without a prescription. Defendant admitted the gun was hers, and that she knew it was under the mattress. In exchange for defendant's guilty plea, the State agreed to recommend a 36-month sentence, and to not pursue a felon-in-possession of a firearm charge against her. Defendant argued that her sentence under the firearm-enhancement statute, Minn. Stat. § 609.11, subd. 5(a) (2004), violated her right to a jury trial under the U.S. Supreme Court decision in Blakely. The appellate court found that the factual determinations necessary for the sentence enhancement were a violation of defendant's right to a jury trial under Blakely. The presumptive sentence for defendant's offense without the firearm enhancement would have been far less than 36 months. When the district court sentenced defendant to an enhanced term of 36 months, the firearm enhancement functioned as an aggravating factor. Defendant was entitled to have a jury determine whether she possessed the firearm at the time of the drug offense, and whether the firearm's presence increased the risk of violence.


OUTCOME: The sentence was reversed and remanded.

 

416 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Mooney


A04-2375


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 590



June 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Brown v. Mooney, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 461 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by Brown v. Mooney, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 64677 (D. Minn., Sept. 8, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Carlton County; Hon. Robert E. Macaulay, Jr., Judge. District Court File No. CV-04-1014.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, petitioner, challenged the judgment of the Carlton County District Court, Minnesota, denying him a jury trial in his commitment action as a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was 30 years old, and repeatedly sexually assaulted his 11-year old sister from February 1992 through March 1993. The petitioner was 16 years old when the abuse began. During the same time frame, the petitioner molested two of his female cousins. The petitioner also admitted to sexual contact with his uncle's dog, and had several run-ins with the law, including alleged assaults against his parents and a mall security guard. The petitioner pled guilty to first-degree criminal sexual conduct for abusing his sister, and the petitioner was later committed as a sexually dangerous person. The petitioner argued that he was entitled to a jury trial in his civil commitment proceeding. The appellate court ruled that the Minnesota State Constitution did not guarantee a right to a jury trial in a civil commitment proceeding, and there was no federal constitutional right to a jury trial in civil commitment proceedings in the State of Minnesota.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

417 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Minn. Ins. Guar. Ass'n v. Integra Telecom, Inc.


A04-1877


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


697 N.W.2d 223; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 593



June 7, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Minn. Ins. Guar. Ass'n v. Integra Telecom, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 507 (Minn., Aug. 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. 03-14751.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) that granted summary judgment for respondent Minnesota Insurance Guaranty Association (MIGA) on its claim pursuant to the Minnesota Insurance Guaranty Association Act, Minn. Stat. § 60C.01-60C.22 (2002), for the amount paid in settling an employee's workers' compensation claim without the employer's consent after the employer's insurer became insolvent.


OVERVIEW: The employer claimed the trial court erred in construing the MIGA Act to permit the MIGA to maintain a reimbursement claim for the amount paid in a settlement of a workers' compensation claim without the employer's consent; and that Minn. Stat. § 60C.11, subd. 3, prohibited the MIGA from bringing a claim against the employer. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for the MIGA. The court held that an implied authority to settle claims without the insured's consent was inferred from the statutory scheme in light of the broad description of the MIGA's powers in Minn. Stat. § 60C.05, subd. 2(d) and (e); the absence of any consent requirement in Minn. Stat. § 60C.11, subd. 7; and the remedial purpose of the Act. The court held that § 60C.11, subd. 7 was more specific and had been added to the Act more recently, thus it prevailed over § 60C.11, subd. 3, and permitted the MIGA to recover from an insured with a net worth over $ 25 million. The court did not address the employer's challenge of the constitutionality of the Act because the employer failed to notify the attorney general of its challenge as required by Minn. R. Civ. App. P. 144 and the MIGA was not a state agency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that granted summary judgment for the MIGA.

 

418 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Albert


A04-1298


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 611



June 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. John Q. McShane, Judge. District Court. File No. 04026849.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) that convicted him of failure to stop at a stoplight, a violation of Minn. Stat. § 169.89, subds. 1, 2 (2002), and that sentenced him to a fine of $ 300. In his appeal, defendant raised the issues of discriminatory enforcement of traffic laws, rejection of his midtrial request for a continuance to obtain counsel, and the excessiveness of the $ 300 fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the traffic laws were discriminatorily enforced because the police officers did not stop the first car that went through the intersection, which was driven by a white person. The court found that defendant waived his discriminatory enforcement defense because he did not raise the issue before trial. The court noted that even if the issue had been properly raised, defendant failed to show that he was singled out based on an impermissible classification. The record provided two logical, nondiscriminatory reasons for stopping defendant's car and provided no evidence that the officers knew of the other driver's race. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's continuance request as untimely and in concluding that it was an attempt to delay the proceedings because defendant stated that he was representing himself and he had a full opportunity to secure an attorney or to request a continuance before trial began, but waited until the State completed its case in chief. Also, the fine was not excessive because it was not disproportionate to the gravity of the offense or the penalty imposed for similar offenses in Minnesota and in other states.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment, holding that defendant failed to timely raise or prove discriminatory enforcement, the denial of the continuance was within the trial court's discretion, and the fine was not excessive.

 

419 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Haumant v. Griffin


A04-1746


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


699 N.W.2d 774; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 621



June 7, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Haumant v. Griffin, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 528 (Minn., Aug. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. MC 04-13463.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen challenged a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) that denied his request for an injunction requiring respondent city elections director to place a proposed charter amendment regarding medical marijuana distribution centers on the city's general-election ballot.


OVERVIEW: The citizen sought to have a charter amendment placed on the ballot that would require the city to authorize and regulate medical marijuana distribution centers. The trial court denied the citizen's request for an injunction based on its finding that the amendment was unconstitutional, preempted by state and federal law, and was an improper initiative rather than an amendment. The citizen argued that where the technical requirements for amendment proposals had been met, the city had a mandatory duty to place all proposed charter amendments on the ballot. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court judgment. The court found that the amendment was subject to the doctrine of preemption and the judicially-created requirement that proposed charter provisions not be "manifestly unconstitutional." The court found that the legislature, by virtue of Minn. Stat. §§ 152.021-.029, had indicated its intent to occupy the field of marijuana regulation and, thus, preempted municipal action. The court concluded that the phrase "manifestly unconstitutional" had never been interpreted as barring only those proposed amendments that were proven to be unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that denied the citizen's request for injunctive relief.

 

420 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jenkins


A04-698


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 625



June 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Jenkins, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 541 (Minn., Aug. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County; Hon. Steven D. Wheeler, Judge. District Court File No. K3-03-217.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) that denied his motion to suppress and convicted him of fifth-degree possession of a controlled substance (marijuana), a violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.025, subd. 2(1) and 3(a) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the police conducting surveillance at a bar for an unrelated controlled buy who saw defendant meet a man outside the bar and give him a package did not have articulable suspicion to seize defendant by asking him to leave the bar and answer questions. Defendant also claimed that the officers did not have reasonable suspicion to justify a pat down and that they exceed the permissible scope of a pat down. The court affirmed the trial court judgment. The court found that the officers had reasonable suspicion to seize defendant and perform a pat down because they saw him give the man a package after talking on his cell phone, he was at a bar that had a long history of drug traffic and shootings, and his behavior was "suspicious" under the circumstances. The court rejected defendant's claim that the pat search exceeded the permissible boundaries of a Terry stop because although there was conflicting evidence regarding whether the officer patted or squeezed the bulge in defendant's clothes, the officer did not manipulate the package in an unconstitutionally improper way and the officer could seize what he believed to be contraband under the "plain feel" exception.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

421 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lopez


A05-63


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 640



June 7, 2005, Decided  
June 14, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Lopez, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 709 (Minn., Nov. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Rice County; Hon. Bernard E. Borene, Judge. District Court File No. K7041514.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment of the Rice County District Court (Minnesota), which denied the State's motion to add a charge of second-degree controlled-substance crime to its complaint against defendant. The State argued that defendant's alleged sale of drugs took place in a "park zone" as required by Minn. Stat. § 152.022, subd. 1(6)(i) (2002).


OVERVIEW: The State asserted that the mobile home from which defendant allegedly sold drugs was on the same "city block" as a municipal park and that the southernmost portion of the mobile-home court in which defendant's mobile home was located was within 300 feet of the municipal park, satisfying the element in that the alleged sale took place within a park zone. The district court held, as a matter of law, that the alleged sale did not take place in a park zone. The court determined that the area described by the State did not meet the definition of a city block because it was only bounded on two sides by streets or avenues. The court also determined that it was clear from the aerial photograph in the record that the mobile home from which the alleged sale was made was not within one city block of the park. The State's focus on the location of the mobile-home court rather than the location of the sale was misplaced because the statute required that the sale had to occur within the park zone in order for the statute to apply. Because it was undisputed that the sale occurred more than 300 feet from the park, the trial court did not err in denying the State's motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Lawrence


A04-1871


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 541



May 24, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dakota County; Hon. Robert Carolan, Judge. District Court File No. K6041207.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of fifth-degree controlled-substance offense. On appeal, defendant challenged the district court's pretrial order denying his motion to suppress evidence. He argued that the search warrant at issue was not supported by probable cause and the police illegally seized his garbage.


OVERVIEW: A confidential informant told the county drug task force that an individual, identified as defendant, was selling methamphetamine from his residence. A police officer retrieved the household garbage defendant had left in a container outside his residence for pickup by a contracted sanitation service. Police searched the garbage and discovered items containing methamphetamine residue. On the basis of this discovery, and the fact that defendant had two previous controlled-substance convictions, the sheriff's department obtained a search warrant. Defendant argued that the information provided by the confidential informant did not provide probable cause to issue the search warrant because the State did not establish the informant's reliability. The record was clear that although the confidential informant gave the information leading to the garbage search, probable cause for the warrant was provided by the discovery of methamphetamine residue in defendant's garbage. The court then noted that there was no evidence defendant took any steps to protect the area or the container from passers-by. Defendant did not have a reasonable expectation of privacy in the container.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Gouleed


A04-700


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 551



May 24, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Gouleed, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 522 (2005)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by State v. Gouleed, 720 N.W.2d 794, 2006 Minn. LEXIS 624 (Minn., Sept. 7, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County; Hon. Gary W. Bastian, Judge. File No. K3-02-4161.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) of second-degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: During trial, it came to light that defendant's expert had done some additional work on a slide that was never disclosed. The prosecutor stated that he had seen some of the slides for the first time during the expert testimony and that the slides were of critical importance because the expert was using them to date the injuries. The trial court, sua sponte, granted a mistrial. Defendant argued, inter alia, that his retrial was barred on double-jeopardy grounds because a mistrial was not a manifest necessity in his first trial. The court of appeals agreed. A clarification of the expert's testimony as to how many of the slides contained his own iron staining, the limitation of his further testimony about his own tests, the striking of testimony about his own tests, a cautionary instruction, a short continuance to allow the State's expert to review the tests, and rebuttal testimony were a few of the obvious alternatives to a mistrial. Those would have been reasonable options, considering the inescapable fact that there simply was no dispute about the existence of old blood and previous head trauma.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

424 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Fedziuk v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety


A04-2328


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


696 N.W.2d 340; 2005 Minn. LEXIS 271



May 19, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Dakota County. Office of Appellate Courts.
Fedziuk v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 41 (Minn., Jan. 20, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered; motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Minnesota Department of Public Safety sustained the revocation of respondent driver's license after administrative review. The driver sought a declaratory judgment and asked a Minnesota district court to hold that the Implied Consent Law (amended 2003) violated procedural due process. The district court determined that the Implied Consent Law's prehearing revocation procedures violated due process. Two questions were certified.


OVERVIEW: The driver was arrested for driving while impaired. A schedule II substance was found in the driver's blood. The driver raised the defense that the drug was prescribed. The two questions certified for review were (1) whether the current version of the implied consent scheme violated due process and (2) whether the 1980 version of the law was revived, and if not, what version was revived? The supreme court was required to determine whether immediately available administrative review, combined with an unspecified period for judicial review, provided a sufficiently meaningful postrevocation review that protected the driver's due process rights. The supreme court determined that the 2003 amendments to Minnesota's Implied Consent Law were unconstitutional because there was no requirement in the amendments that a review hearing be prompt; therefore, the 2003 amendments eliminated a critical due process element to the Implied Consent Law. The supreme court's answer to the second part of the second certified question was that the version of the Implied Consent Law that was revived was the version that existed immediately prior to the 2003 amendments.


OUTCOME: The supreme court answered the certified questions by determining that the 2003 amendments were unconstitutionally violative of due process and that the version of the Implied Consent that was revived was the one that existed immediately prior to the 2003 amendments. The driver's motion to strike the Commissioner's brief and for fees and costs was denied.

In re Civil Commitment of Foley


A04-2340


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 534



May 17, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Civil Commitment of: Foley, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 460 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Renville County; Hon. Randall J. Slieter, Judge. District Court File No. P9-04-64.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Renville County District Court (Minnesota) that committed him as a sexually dangerous person (SDP) under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18c (2004) and as a sexual psychopathic personality (SPP) under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18b (2004), based on the trial court's findings that he was highly likely to reoffend and could not control his impulses.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed the record did not support the findings that he was likely to reoffend or that he could not control his impulses, and that his commitment violated double jeopardy and due process. The court affirmed the trial court judgment, holding that there was clear and convincing evidence to support defendant's commitment as an SDP and an SPP. The court found that even though the experts differed in their opinion, both experts testified that defendant received high scores on tests that were above the cutoff for a clinical psychopath and reflected a high likelihood of violent re-offense. Also defendant failed to appreciate the seriousness of his offenses and the need for treatment. The court noted that the Minnesota Supreme Court has rejected the argument that the SDP and SPP statutes violated double jeopardy, and has held that as long as civil commitment was programmed to provide treatment and periodic review, due process was provided. The court noted that the trial court had made significant changes to the State's proposed findings and that verbatim adoption of proposed findings was not reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

State v. Olson


A04-1152


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 489



May 10, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Blue Earth County; Hon. Bradley C. Walker, Judge. District Court File No. K0-03-963.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Blue Earth County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of aiding and abetting the following crimes: robbery in the first degree, kidnapping, assault in the second degree, and terroristic threats. On appeal, defendant challenged the district court's refusal to suppress the evidence and dismiss the charges.


OVERVIEW: Police went to search defendant's apartment. The warrant did not describe the items to be seized. Upon entering defendant's apartment, the lead officer returned to court to obtain an amended warrant to expand the search area. The amended warrant also failed to include a description of the items to be seized. While the lead officer was gone, defendant's acquaintance brought a videotape to the apartment. When the waiting officers asked about the tape, the acquaintance gave it to them. The officers viewed the tape, which recorded defendant robbing, assaulting, and holding an unidentified man at defendant's apartment for several hours. On appeal, the State conceded that the warrant was invalid, that the search of defendant's apartment was unconstitutional, that the tape should not have been admitted into evidence, and that the convictions should be reversed. Despite the State's concession, the court conducted an independent analysis. It found that because the videotape was obtained during a search for which the warrant was invalid, the tape was "fruit of the poisonous tree." The court determined that there were not independent means that would purge the primary taint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter to the district court.

 

427 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


A04-783


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 491



May 10, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County; Hon. Paulette K. Flynn, Judge. District Court File No. K2033920.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his motion to suppress was denied, defendant was convicted of a fifth-degree controlled-substance crime in the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota. He appealed, asserting the warrant for the search of his residence illegally authorized an unannounced entry because the application relied on past arrests for crimes involving weapons and provided no other articulable suspicion to support a no-knock provision.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the record showed the supporting affidavit stated that a confidential reliable informant (CRI) had seen defendant in possession of substantial amounts of marijuana. Further, shortly before the application for the warrant, defendant sold marijuana to a CRI. The affidavit also listed crimes for which defendant previously had been arrested, which included aggravated robbery, second-degree assault with a dangerous weapon, and possession of a machine gun and/or short-barreled shotguns. Thus, the magistrate issued a search warrant authorizing an unannounced entry. The appellate court noted that to justify an unannounced entry, police had to have a reasonable suspicion that knocking and announcing their presence, under the particular circumstances, would be dangerous or futile, or that it would inhibit an effective investigation by, for example, allowing the destruction of evidence. The latter standard was less than a probable cause standard. The mere presence of firearms alone did not suffice under the reasonable suspicion standard, but defendant's violent criminal history, in conjunction with said weapons, raised a concern for officer safety and allowed for a no-knock search.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Berry


A04-1435


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 455



May 3, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Berry, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 452 (2005)
Appeal after remand at State v. Berry, 2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 901 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. Marilyn Brown Rosenbaum, Judge. District Court File No. 03061085.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, sentenced defendant under the dangerous-offender statute to consecutive upward durational departures on two counts of first-degree burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to consecutive sentences of 120 months on the first count, which was a double durational departure from the presumptive sentence, and 60 months on the second count, which was an upward departure from the 21-month presumptive sentence. The appellate court ruled that the upward durational departures were constitutionally invalid under the U.S. Supreme Court Blakely decision. The district court based its dangerous-offender departure on judicial findings that defendant was a danger to public safety, had a high-frequency rate of offending, and had a long criminal history. The district court also relied on judicial findings that the victim was vulnerable, and that the crime was particularly cruel, both aggravating factors that would justify a departure under the sentencing guidelines. Defendant's sentence exceeded the maximum sentence the district court could impose solely on the basis of the facts reflected in his plea, and the district court relied on facts that were neither admitted by defendant nor found by a jury.


OUTCOME: The consecutive sentencing was affirmed, but the upward durational departures were reversed and the case was remanded for determination of the individual sentences.

State v. Turner


A04-949


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 463



May 3, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Turner, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 438 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. Isabel Gomez, Judge. District Court File No. 03071300.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him of felony driving while impaired (DWI).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by an officer for driving with a broken rear taillight. When the officer approached defendant, the officer smelled alcohol, and noticed that defendant's eyes were glassy and watering. A preliminary breath test showed that defendant's alcohol concentration was .105. Defendant waived his right to a jury trial and agreed to submit the matter to the district court on stipulated facts. Defendant argued that the use of civil license revocations to enhance the criminality of his DWI charge under Minn. Stat. § 169A.24 (2002), violated his constitutional right to due process. The appellate court ruled that the use of civil license revocations to enhance the DWI charge did not violate the right to due process. Judicial review of the civil revocation was available to defendant, but defendant did not seek such review. Meaningful review was available, and the requirement that an alternative means of obtaining review must be made available was satisfied. Minnesota courts had also consistently held that using a prior license revocation as an aggravating factor was not unconstitutional, and defendant sets forth no compelling reason to depart from this judicial precedent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

430 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rettke


A04-1358


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 478



May 3, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Crow Wing County; Hon. Richard A. Zimmerman, Judge. District Court File No. KX-02-2833.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the durational departure sentenced of thirty-six months, an upward durational departure of six months from the presumptive guidelines' sentence, entered by the Crow Wing County District Court, Minnesota, for his conviction of third-degree burglary.


OVERVIEW: The district court determined that the departure was appropriate because defendant and the prosecutor had agreed to the thirty-six-month sentence, defendant had five or more prior felony convictions, and the current offense was a felony that was committed as part of a pattern of criminal conduct. The appellate court ruled that because the factual basis for defendant's sentencing departure was not part of the stipulated facts or the result of a jury determination, the upward durational departure constituted judicial fact-finding, which violated defendant's right to a jury trial. The record did not establish a knowing waiver of defendant's right to a jury determination of the factors that permitted departure under the career-offender statute. Defendant did not stipulate that his current offense constituted a pattern of criminal conduct that justified departure under the career-offender statute. Defendant's acceptance of the thirty-six-month sentence did not constitute a knowing or express waiver of his constitutional right to a jury determination on whether his current offense was committed as part of a pattern of criminal conduct.


OUTCOME: The sentence was reversed and remanded.

State v. Khang Yang


A04-1274


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 432



April 26, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County; Hon. Jenny Walker Jasper, Judge. District Court File No. K1-04-954.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), which imposed a double durational departure and a consecutive sentence after he pled guilty to burglary and two counts of assault.


OVERVIEW: After pleading guilty, defendant was sentenced to a presumptive term of 27 months in prison for first-degree burglary, 54 months for second-degree assault involving one victim, which represented a double durational departure; and 21 months for second-degree assault of another victim. The trial court ordered the 54-month assault sentence to be served concurrently with the burglary sentence, and the 21-month assault sentence to be served consecutively. On appeal, defendant challenged the upward departure and the imposition of a consecutive sentence. The court found that even if defendant's guilty plea could be read to include admissions to support findings on the aggravating factors, his plea did not include a waiver of his right to a jury trial on the sentencing factors. Thus, the trial court erred in imposing a departure. The court further found, however, that the trial court's decision to impose consecutive sentences did not violate defendant's Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the consecutive sentence. The court reversed the decision to depart and remanded the case for resentencing.

Concept Props., LLP v. City of Minnetrista


A04-1414


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


694 N.W.2d 804; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 418



April 19, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Concept Props., LLP v. City of Minnetrista, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 449 (2005)



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property company sought review of a decision of a district court (Minnesota), which entered summary judgment for appellee city in the company's action to have land that had been removed from the Metropolitan Urban Services Area (MUSA), returned to the MUSA and rezoned for residential development at urban densities.


OVERVIEW: The land had been formerly assessed for a sewer system when the city assessed all properties that were located within the MUSA. As of January 1997, the property was no longer within the MUSA. The court held: (1) earlier inclusion of the property in the MUSA did not preclude the city from removing the property from the MUSA at a later date; (2) the city's decision to amend its comprehensive plan to comport with directives from the metropolitan council was not arbitrary or capricious; (3) both objectives sought by the company were inconsistent with the city's policies of preserving the city's rural character and preventing urban sprawl, as such, a legally sufficient rationale supported the city's denial of the company's application to amend the comprehensive plan and rezone the subject property; (4) although the inability to connect to the sewer made development of the subject property more difficult, it did not deny the property all reasonable use, and thus the company's takings claim failed; and (5) the city did not violate the company's substantive due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the city.

 

433 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Weston v. McWilliams & Assocs.


A04-1251


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


694 N.W.2d 558; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 395



April 12, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by McWilliams & Assocs. v. Tappe Constr., 2005 Minn. LEXIS 371 (2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by Weston v. McWilliams & Assocs., 716 N.W.2d 634, 2006 Minn. LEXIS 400 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Dakota County District Court. File No. C3-03-010176.
Weston v. McWilliams & Assocs., 2004 Minn. Dist. LEXIS 12 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the underlying action, plaintiff, a homeowner, sued defendant, a contractor for defective construction just before the tenth anniversary of the completion of the home. After said tenth year, the contractor then sued third party defendants, three subcontractors, for contribution and indemnity. The Dakota County District Court, Minnesota, held the contractor's claims were barred by a statute of repose. The contractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issue was whether the district court correctly determined that Minn. Stat. § 541.051, subd. 1(a) (2002), barred initiation of a contribution and indemnity suit in the 11th year after completion of said construction. The appellate court noted that § 541.051, subd. 1(a) (providing for a 10 year limitation period), was a statute of repose added to the statute of limitation, declaring an ultimate repose of a contribution or indemnity action, regardless of when the cause of action arose. On the other hand, Minn. Stat. § 541.051, subd. 2 (2002), provided that no action of the kind addressed by Minn. Stat. § 541.051, subd. 1 (2002) could "be brought" more than 12 years after construction was completed. After examining legislative intent, and seeking to avoid an absurd interpretation, the appellate court held that Minn. Stat. § 541.051, subd. 1(a) (2002) deemed accrual of a party's contribution and indemnity claims to "occur at the end of the 10th year" following completion of construction. Further, because § 541.051, subd. 1(a) permitted commencement of action on the claims in the following two years after "discovery of the injury," the contractor's actions were timely.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

 

434 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hanks


A04-826


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 403



April 12, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Becker County; Hon. Thomas P. Schroeder, Judge. District Court File No. KX-03-885.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Becker County District Court, Minnesota, on two counts of felony first-degree driving while impaired (DWI). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Prior to trial, defendant pleaded guilty to driving-after-cancellation and stipulated to his cancellation to avoid the jury hearing evidence concerning his driving record. At trial, the police officer testified without objection that defendant was "cancelled." Defendant argued that the trial court erred by admitting prejudicial statements regarding his driving record, and that a White Earth Tribal Police Officer lacked the authority to stop, detain, or search him. The appellate court held that the testimony regarding defendant's driving record was improper because of the strong inference that his cancellation was due to a prior DWI conviction; however, he was not automatically entitled to reversal because he failed to show that he was so prejudiced by the admission of the officer's "cancelled" testimony that he did not receive a fair trial. The appellate court further held that the law-enforcement arrangement between the State of Minnesota and the White Earth Tribal Police Force did not violate federal law or the constitution; thus, evidence derived from the officer's stop, search, and seizure of defendant and his vehicle was properly admitted.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

435 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mancini


A03-1455


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 391



April 12, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Stay granted by State v. Mancini, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 413 (2005)
Review denied by State v. Mancini, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 767 (Minn., Dec. 13, 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Stay denied by, Motion denied by, Motion denied by, As moot Mancini v. State, 2015 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 341 (Minn. Ct. App., Apr. 13, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County; Hon. Kathleen R. Gearin, Judge. District Court File Nos. K0-02- 4361 & K2-02-4314.
State v. Mancini, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 651 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to second and third-degree criminal sexual conduct, and challenged the order of the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, sentencing him to 38 months for the third-degree criminal sexual conduct conviction and a consecutive 90 months for the second-degree criminal sexual conduct conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the district court violated his Sixth Amendment rights by including a custody-status point in his criminal-history score when it calculated the presumptive sentence for his conviction of third-degree criminal sexual conduct. The district court included a custody-status point because it found that defendant was on probation when he committed the offense. Defendant argued that the U.S. Supreme Court Blakely decision required a jury determination that he was on probation because it was a fact that increased his sentence. The appellate court ruled that the district court did not err by including a custody-status point in defendant's criminal-history score and imposing the presumptive sentence for his third-degree criminal-sexual-conduct conviction. A finding of a custody-status point fit within Blakely's exception for facts of prior convictions. Also, the district court did not violate defendant's Sixth Amendment right to a jury as described in Blakely by finding that his offenses were "crimes against persons" and imposing consecutive sentences.


OUTCOME: The sentences were affirmed.

 

436 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Unity Church v. State


A04-1302


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


694 N.W.2d 585; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 390



April 12, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Edina Cmty. Lutheran Church v. State, 2006 Minn. Dist. LEXIS 44 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court. File No. C9-03-9570.
Edina Cmty. Lutheran Church v. State, 673 N.W.2d 517, 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 17 (2004)
Unity Church of St. Paul v. State, 2004 Minn. Dist. LEXIS 18 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, religious and charitable organizations, filed suit challenging the constitutionality of provisions of the Minnesota Citizens' Personal Protection Act of 2003 (PPA) under 2003 Minn. Laws. ch. 28. The Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) held that the PPA violated the single-subject requirement of Minn. Const. art. IV, § 17 and severed it from the chapter. Appellant State sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State contended, inter alia, that 2003 Minn. Laws ch. 28 did not violate the single-subject requirement of Minn. Const. art. IV, § 17. The appellate court disagreed, finding that 2003 Minn. Laws ch. 28, arts. 2-3 related to handgun permitting and firearm regulation, while 2003 Minn. Laws ch. 28, art. 1 related to the single subject of natural resources or the environment. Thus, the two disparate subjects lacked a legitimate connection to one another and failed the germaneness analysis. As such, the appellate court held that 2003 Minn. Laws ch. 28 was unconstitutional in violation of the single-subject requirement. The appellate court agreed with the trial court's determination that severance of 2003 Minn. Laws ch. 28, arts. 2-3 was appropriate, thus, bringing 2003 Minn. Laws. ch. 28 into constitutional compliance with Minn. Const. art. IV, § 17.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

437 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson


A04-1808


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


694 N.W.2d 117; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 337



April 5, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Thompson, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 374 (2005)
Reversed by State v. Thompson, 720 N.W.2d 820, 2006 Minn. LEXIS 623 (Minn., Sept. 7, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. 03090707.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, which upon defendant's guilty plea to nine counts of theft by swindle under Minn. Stat. § 609.52, subds. 2(4), 3(1), (5) (2002), sentenced her to the presumptive sentence on counts one to four and imposed concurrent sentences of 114 months on counts five to nine.


OVERVIEW: After being terminated by her employer, defendant voluntarily admitted to substantially all allegations of embezzlement. She pleaded guilty to nine counts in a straight plea. Defendant charged that the upward departure of her sentence violated her right to a jury trial under Blakely. The court noted that under Blakely, an upward durational departure could not be based on an admission by defendant unless it was accompanied by defendant's waiver of her right to a jury trial on the aggravating factor. The court held that defendant orally waived her right to a jury trial but that she did not explicitly acknowledge and waiver her right to testify and to have prosecution witnesses testify. Therefore, the record was not sufficient to demonstrate that defendant knowingly waived those rights. The court also held that defendant was not automatically entitled on remand to a reduction of her sentence to the presumptive sentence. Because the appropriate remedy, including the possible impaneling of a jury to determine the sentencing issues, had not been fully litigated, it had to be determined in the first instance by the district court.


OUTCOME: The court held that the district court erred in sentencing defendant and remanded for further proceedings.

In re Civ. Commitment of: Grabowska


A04-1944


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 339



April 5, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. Patricia L. Belois, Judge. District Court File No. MH-PR-04-000758.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, determined that appellant patient was mentally ill and committed him. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued that the evidence did not support the determination that he had a substantial psychiatric disorder that posed a substantial likelihood of physical harm to himself or others or that commitment was the least-restrictive alternative. The appellate court noted that pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 13(a)(1), (3) (2004), the requirement of a showing of a likelihood of harm was crucial because a mentally ill person's confinement was unconstitutional if he was dangerous to no one and could live safely in freedom. The appellate court agreed with the patient that the findings regarding his inability to obtain necessities were insufficient. The district court made no findings on the patient's failure to take his medication consistently. The patient's verbal confrontations with others, without more, were insufficient to show that there was a substantial likelihood of physical harm to himself or others, as required.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for further findings.

 

439 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Moreno v. State


A04-1196


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 372



April 5, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Moreno v. State, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 398 (Minn., June 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Brown County; Hon. John E. Pearson, Judge. District Court. File No. K6-98-23.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: While serving a sentence for a controlled-substance crime in another county, half of appellant inmate's wages were deducted to pay a fine arising from a conviction in the instant county for which he already served his jail sentence. The Brown County District Court, Minnesota, denied the inmate's motion for postconviction relief in which he argued that appellee department of corrections lacked authority to make the deductions. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the inmate challenged the denial of his postconviction petition, arguing that the trial court properly asserted jurisdiction over his claim because fines were a direct consequence of a conviction. The appellate court found that defendant did not challenge the judgment of conviction nor did he challenge the trial court's imposition of the fine as part of his sentence. Rather, he challenged the department's authority to collect wages for payment of the fine, contending that Minn. Stat. § 243.23, subd. 3 (2002) did not grant authority to the department to collect wages for payment of a fine arising from a sentence that had expired. Because defendant's challenge related to a condition of his confinement and was not a challenge to the judgment of conviction or the imposed sentence, the appellate court held that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to consider defendant's unauthorized-deduction claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
