Thompson v. State


A04-941


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 249



March 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. Marilyn Brown Rosenbaum, Judge. District Court File No. 93013570.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of first-degree criminal sexual conduct and sentenced him to 300 months, an upward durational departure from the presumptive 146 months in prison. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on appeal. Defendant petitioned for postconviction relief, arguing that his sentence was unconstitutional under Blakely. The petition was denied, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant argued that the sentencing judge's findings regarding aggravating circumstances should have been tried to a jury. The appellate court found that because defendant took his direct appeal 7 and 11 years respectively before Apprendi and Blakely were decided, it was impossible for him to have raised (or even to have had knowledge about) the precise sentencing issue in those cases and on appeal in his case. However, because defendant's conviction was final before Apprendi and Blakely were decided, the new rules established by those cases were inapplicable. Thus, denial of defendant's motion for postconviction relief was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

441 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Doll v. Barnell (In re Doll)


A04-925, A04-1146


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


693 N.W.2d 455; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 250



March 22, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Review denied by, Motion denied by In re Doll, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 340 (Minn., June 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Stearns County District Court. File No. F5-00-388. Anoka County District Court. File No. F7-97-51337.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Appellant's motion to strike denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two cases, the Stearns County District Court, Minnesota, and the Anoka County District Court, Minnesota, upheld the constitutionality of Minnesota's Child Support Guidelines. Appellant fathers challenged the decisions. The matters were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: Both fathers argued that Minnesota's child-support guidelines violated the United States Constitution's Supremacy, Due Process, and Equal Protection Clauses because the child-support guidelines impacted their fundamental right to control their care of their children. There was no precedent cited, however, holding that one parent had a fundamental right over the other parent in respect to child-support obligations. There was also no merit in the argument that gender was implicated in the statutory scheme. There was also no merit to the claim that courts mechanically look to the child support guidelines. As to the Equal Protection Clause analysis, the fathers failed to make the threshold showing that they, as noncustodians, were similarly situated with respect to the custodians. Moreover, the legislature was well within in its constitutional authority in deciding to maximize recovery of child support. As to due process, the legislature allowed for deviations from the guidelines, and the guidelines furthered reasonable objectives. Finally, the fathers failed to show that the existing Minnesota guidelines conflicted with or violate the mandates of federal law.


OUTCOME: An appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

442 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Mulcare v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety


A04-1019


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 252



March 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dakota County; Hon. Martha M. Simonett, Judge. District Court File No. C8-04-12337.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An officer found appellant motorist unconscious and behind the steering wheel of her parked vehicle. Subsequently, the officer invoked the implied consent law, and the motorist's test revealed an alcohol concentration of .10 or more. Her driver's license was revoked by respondent, the Minnesota Commissioner of Public Safety. The Dakota County District Court, Minnesota, affirmed. The motorist appealed, asserting an unconstitutional seizure.


OVERVIEW: At about 2:25 a.m., a clerk at a gas station notified a police dispatcher that a motorist appeared to be sleeping behind the wheel of a van, parked with its motor running, directly in front of the station. The officer arrived, and based on past experience, he suspected the motorist was impaired. On appeal, the motorist first argued, correctly, that she was seized when the officer parked his squad car behind her vehicle, preventing her exit. However, the primary issue was whether the officer had a reasonable, articulable suspicion to justify the investigative seizure, primarily with respect to the clerk's tip. Although not identified by name, the dispatcher knew the caller was a clerk at the gas station, and the officer could have easily identified the caller. Therefore, it was unlikely the caller would have provided false information. Because the clerk witnessed the situation first hand, there was a factual basis for her knowledge as an informant. The appellate court held that in conjunction with the officer's personal observations and experience and given the totality of the circumstances, he had a reasonable and articulable suspicion of criminal activity to seize defendant.


OUTCOME: The revocation of the motorist's license was affirmed.

In re McRae

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of the decision of the trial court (Minnesota), which found sufficient evidence to support his commitment as a sexually dangerous person.


OVERVIEW: The individual challenged the constitutionality of the sexually dangerous person statute, Minn. 444 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


ILHC of Eagan, LLC v. County of Dakota


A03-1407


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


693 N.W.2d 412; 2005 Minn. LEXIS 113



March 17, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tax Court. Clerk of Appellate Courts.
ILHC of Eagan, LLC v. County of Dakota, 2003 Minn. Tax LEXIS 13 (Minn. T.C., May 1, 2003).



DISPOSITION: Tax Court judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator county petitioned for a writ of certiorari to the Minnesota Tax Court, which concluded that petitioner taxpayer was eligible for a partial property tax exemption under former Minn. Stat. § 272.02, subd. 26 (2002), and granted summary judgment in favor of the taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was an assisted living facility. The question was whether § 272.02, subd. 26(D) limited the exemption to housing that existed and was unassessed before the 1991 tax levy and whether § 272.02, subd. 26(ii) limited the exemption to housing for low-income residents. The court held that the "while" clause within § 272.02, subd. 26(D) established a time relationship and that the provision required a structure situated on real property to have been in existence before the 1991 tax levy to be eligible for a tax exemption. The taxpayer was not eligible for exemption under § 272.02, subd. 26(D). Also, the purpose was to create a remedy for those properties affected by a tax increase that affected the ability of low-income housing property owners to offer affordable rents to tenants. Further, the time cutoff at 1991 was reasonably related to the statute's remedial purpose of allowing the affected properties a partial exemption for reasonably unanticipated property tax increases, and the partial exemption provided in § 272.02, subd. 26 was rational because the sudden increase in taxes could enforce a hardship on those properties' ability to provide low-income housing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the tax court.

 

445 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kuehn


A04-815


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 259



March 16, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Washington County; Hon. Mary E. Carlson, Judge. District Court File No. T9-03-20259.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for passing another vehicle on the right. He appealed, asserting that the Washington County District Court, Minnesota, abused its discretion by excluding impeachment evidence showing that the officer who wrote the citation was biased against defendant's employer, whose truck he was driving at the time of the incident. He also asserted the trial court misconstrued the applicable statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was cited for violating Minn. Stat. § 169.18, subd. 4 (2002), by passing on the shoulder. He based his bias theory on a lawsuit the officer had brought against his employer. The suit was pending at the time of the traffic stop and alleged that a fence that the company installed on the officer's property had failed to restrain the officer's dog, leading to the dog's death. The trial court sustained the State's relevance objections to the documents and the testimony of defendant's witnesses in the latter regard. But defendant's attorney was allowed to establish the nature of said lawsuit. The appellate court held defendant was able to present his theory of bias during cross-examination, and that pursuant to Minn. R. Evid. 608(b), the trial court did not abuse its discretion by excluding the extrinsic evidence defendant proposed to use for impeachment. The appellate court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court misconstrued Minn. Stat. § 169.18, subd. 4 (2002), and that the statute was to be read to include the shoulder of a road as part of "the main-traveled portion of the roadway." Driving on the shoulder to pass another vehicle was a violation of the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Voss


A04-1035


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 200



March 1, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Polk County; Hon. Dennis J. Murphy, Judge and Hon. Richard C. Taylor, Judge. District Court File No. T6-03-2963.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Polk County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of fourth-degree driving while intoxicated under Minn. Stat. § 169A.20, subd. 1(5) (2002) following a trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the district court erred in not dismissing the charge because the evidence against him was obtained after the initial scope of the stop was unconstitutionally expanded. The appellate court noted that defendant made no attempt to argue that the stop was illegal and the appellate court deemed any question regarding the legality of the stop to be waived. Although the police officer did not need an articulable reason to order defendant out of the car, in order to properly conduct the search for the bat-type weapon, defendant was justified in requesting the individuals step out of the car. The officer was justified in confining defendant for the officer's safety because the individuals were suspected of having recently been involved in a potentially violent crime with a possible bat-type weapon. It was reasonable for the officer to confine defendant in the back seat of a squad car while a search for the bat-type weapon was conducted. During the detention, the officer detected the odor of an alcoholic beverage coming from defendant. Thus, there was a continued basis to detain defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Nelson


A04-1126


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 203



March 1, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Redwood County; Hon. David W. Peterson, Judge. District Court District Court File No. KX-03-135.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Redwood County District Court, Minnesota, for the offenses of terroristic threats, interference with a 911 call, domestic assault, and obstructing legal process. He was sentenced to 45 months in prison, but the trial court stayed execution of the prison sentence and placed him on probation. Thereafter, the trial court revoked defendant's probation and sentenced him to 30 months in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions stemmed from an incident at his estranged wife's home. As part of defendant's probationary sentence, the trial court specifically prohibited him from having contact with the victim. Defendant's probation officer later filed a violation report alleging that defendant had placed telephone calls to the victim's residence and lied about the calls when asked by the probation officer. On appeal, defendant challenged the trial court's revocation of his probation, arguing that he had no prior probation violations, that his violations were technical, and that a sanction short of imprisonment was reasonable. The appellate court held that to revoke probation, the trial court had to identify the probationary condition(s) that were violated, find that any violations were intentional or inexcusable, and balance the need for confinement with policies favoring probation. The appellate court found that the trial court's revocation order properly evaluated the probation revocation factors and correctly determined that defendant violated his probation when he telephoned the victim's residence and when he lied about the calls to his probation officer.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Crow


A04-254


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 186



February 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Crow, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 285 (Minn., May 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Redwood County; Hon. David W. Peterson, Judge. District Court File No. K9-03-28.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of third-degree criminal sexual conduct. The Redwood County District Court, Minnesota, sentenced defendant to 120 months, an upward departure from the presumptive sentence of 51 months for third-degree criminal sexual conduct, and ordered the sentence to run concurrently to the 84-month sentence defendant was already serving and dismissed two pending charges. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the time of his conviction, defendant was serving an 84-month sentence for aiding and abetting kidnapping, false imprisonment, and coercion. In addition, defendant had charges pending against him for third-degree assault and escape from custody. Defendant argued that the upward durational departure violated his Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial as defined by the U.S. Supreme Court in Blakely. The appellate court ruled that there was nothing in the record, other than the statement of defendant's counsel at the sentencing hearing that defendant had given up his right to have a contested hearing over the upward departure, to indicate that defendant knowingly waived his right to a jury trial. The State argued that defendant's agreement to the upward departure should suffice as a waiver; however, an upward durational departure could not be based on defendant's admission to an aggravating factor unless the admission was accompanied by defendant's oral or written waiver of his or her right to a jury trial on the aggravating factor. Also, the district court did not err in imposing a ten-year conditional release.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was reversed and the matter was remanded. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.

State v. Seeber


A04 -560


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 193



February 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County; Hon. Kathleen R. Gearin, Judge. District Court File No. T1-03-479911.
Reihsen v. Seeber, 2000 Minn. App. LEXIS 904 (Minn. Ct. App., Aug. 22, 2000).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him of driving after suspension, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 171.24, subd. 1 (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's driver's license was suspended for failure to pay child support, and defendant was later cited for driving with a suspended license. Defendant, on appeal from the criminal conviction of driving after suspension, challenged the propriety of the order suspending his driver's license. Defendant contested the administrative agency's statutory authority to suspend his license, however, the appellate court ruled that the challenge constituted an impermissible collateral attack on the administrative order. A challenge to an administrative order suspending defendant's driver's license pursued during an appeal from a later criminal conviction for driving after suspension constituted an impermissible collateral attack on the judgment. Also, since defendant committed a criminal offense in Ramsey County, Minnesota, the trial court properly exercised its jurisdiction over the subject matter. Furthermore, defendant's due process rights were not violated by the absence of written findings or a memorandum of law. The district court made oral findings, and these findings were more than adequate to permit appellate review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

451 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Real Estate Salesperson's License of Grant


A04 -1095


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 196



February 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Minnesota Department of Commerce. File No. 3-1005-15699-2.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Based on allegations of equity stripping, the Minnesota Attorney General brought an action against relators, two real estate sales and mortgage originator licensees and their company (hereinafter, the company). The district court then issued a temporary injunction. Later, respondent, the Commissioner for the Minnesota Department of Commerce, suspended the company's license. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company was alleged to have engaged in a fraudulent practice which targeted homeowners with substantial equity in their homes who were facing foreclosure. The company asserted that the Commissioner's notice violated procedural due process and that he erroneously considered conduct underlying the temporary injunction, rather than the fact of the injunction itself. However, the record showed that the notice cited to both Minn. Stat. § 82.27, subd. 1 (2002) and Minn. Stat. § 58.12, subd. 1 (2002), and those statutes plainly stated that when a licensee was subject to discipline as a result of an injunction, the consequences could include the revocation or suspension. Thus, the company had adequate notice. The appellate court rejected the company's argument, that because the basis for the disciplinary action was the underlying injunction, that the requirements of procedural due process were not satisfied. Again, the company was informed of the potential consequences. Moreover, the company had stipulated to the entire injunction order. Consequently, the Commissioner properly adopted the findings of the district court. Finally, the sanction imposed was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower tribunal was affirmed.

 

452 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Blumer v. Dakota County Cmty. Dev. Agency


A03-1702


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 166



February 15, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dakota County Community Development Authority



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Dakota County, Minnesota, Community Development Agency (CDA), upheld a hearing officer's decision to terminate relator tenant's Section 8 housing benefits based on her failure to report household income. Reports indicated that the tenant's companion began to receive social security payments in 2001, but that he failed to report such income to the CDA on the tenant's subsequent recertification applications. The tenant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tenant had received Section 8 assistance since 1981. When the tenant's companion moved in with her in July 2001, they both applied for a family townhome. However, in meetings with the CDA, they did not mention the companion's social-security income. Further, they did not mention the companion's social-security income on 2002 and 2003 recertification applications. The tenant argued that her benefits should not have been cancelled where the CDA did not prove that her failure to comply with registration requirements was "willful," and that she was not given notice of income-reporting mistakes on her registration or 10 days to correct those mistakes. However, the appellate court held that under the applicable regulations, there was no requirement that a failure to comply with Section 8 registration procedures had to be willful, or that an applicant be given an opportunity to correct mistakes in reported income within 10 days. The responsibility to provide true and complete information regarding income rested with the family pursuant to 24 C.F.R. § 982.551(b). Finally, contrary to her argument, the tenant was provided with an opportunity to contest the cancellation of her benefits.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

In re Civ. Commitment of Martin


A04-1634


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 169



February 15, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Civ. Commitment of Martin, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 239 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Martin v. Benson, 2010 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1009 (Minn. Ct. App., Sept. 28, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County; Hon. Daniel Kammeyer, Judge. District Court File No. PX-01-9959.
In re Civ. Commitment of Martin, 661 N.W.2d 632, 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 602 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), which committed him as a sexually dangerous person (SDP) under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18c (2004).


OVERVIEW: On remand from the district court's denial of the County's petition to commit appellant, the district court concluded that the elements of an SDP case were established where a psychologist testified that he revised his opinion and believed that appellant was highly likely to engage in further sexually motivated stalking behavior. The court affirmed and held following the court's previous opinion, that although appellant did not have physical sexual contact with his victims, his stalking behaviour constituted harmful sexual conduct. The court noted that in the original case, it was determined that he lacked the ability to adequately control his sexual impulses. The court held that there was clear and convincing evidence that appellant was likely to re-offend. Also, in following the Linehan factors, the record supported the conclusion that appellant's acts created a substantial likelihood of serious harm and the district court evaluated the evidence pertaining to each factor. Finally, Minnesota courts have rejected the argument that appellant was entitled to a jury trial because the Minnesota Constitution did not guarantee a right to a jury trial in a civil commitment proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court.

 

454 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Erickson


A04-527


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 184



February 15, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Erickson, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 392 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Beltrami County; Hon. Paul Rasmussen, Judge. District Court File No. K9-03-143.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered into an agreement with the State where he waived his right to a jury trial, agreed to submit a stipulated record to the trial court, and agreed that neither side would be able to cross-examine witnesses. Based on the stipulated record, the Beltrami County District Court, Minnesota, found defendant guilty of refusal to submit to chemical testing under Minn. Stat. § 169A.20, subd. 2 (2002). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that the trial court violated his right to present a defense of reasonable refusal by excluding testimony regarding the basis for his refusal to submit to the chemical test. The appellate court disagreed, finding that defendant was allowed to present such evidence at trial, which was reflected in the stipulated record that was before the trial court; bad legal advice was not a valid excuse for refusing to submit to a chemical test. Defendant's ignorance of the consequences of his actions was not a defense. The fact that there was a less-demanding standard for an officer to stop someone suspected of driving under the influence than there was for the same suspect to be later found guilty at trial did not in any way impinge defendant's constitutional guarantee of due process. Defendant's argument that he was not given sufficient warning as to the consequences of his refusal to test failed, as he stipulated that the Implied Consent Advisory was read to him, that the advisory stated that refusal to submit to testing was a crime, and that he was given an opportunity to speak with an attorney before deciding whether to submit to testing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

455 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Peterson


A04-569


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 143



February 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: St. Louis County; Hon. James B. Florey, Judge. District Court File No. K0-03-101325.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota), which denied a motion to suppress evidence, convicted him of possession of a controlled substance in the fifth degree and obstructing legal process, and assessed him a copayment for public defender services.


OVERVIEW: An informant told police that someone appeared to be tampering with a car at a remote location. When an officer arrived on the scene, he recognized defendant and stopped the car. The officer was erroneously told that there was a warrant for defendant's arrest. During a search, drugs were located. Defendant's motion to suppress was denied, and he sought review. On appeal, the court determined that, despite the informant's statement, the officer did not have specific and articulable facts justifying the stop. However, the evidence obtained during the search was not subject to suppression as "fruit of the poisonous tree." Defendant's act of resisting arrest constituted an intervening circumstance. He was lawfully arrested for obstructing legal process, and the subsequent search was a legal search incident to arrest. However, the court determined that legal fees should not have been charged to defendant under Minn. Stat. § 611.17, subd. 1(c) (Supp. 2003), which had been declared unconstitutional. The court found that defendant could have been required to pay the fees under Minn. R. Crim. P. 5.02, subd. 5 (1999) if there was a finding that he was financially able to make the payment.


OUTCOME: The denial of the motion to suppress was affirmed. The assessment of the copayment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a determination of whether defendant was able to make the payment.

 

456 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Kruger v. Pawlenty


A04-1041


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 104



February 1, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Kruger v. Pawlenty, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 265 (Minn., May 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County; Hon. Judith M. Tilsen, Judge. District Court File No. C2-03-10155.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant detainee sex offenders claimed that the Minn. Stat. § 246.0141 (Supp. 2003) violated a number of constitutional rights under both the United States and Minnesota Constitutions. Respondent governor and respondent commissioner brought a motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim. The district court found for the governor and commissioner and granted the motion. The detainees appealed.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted Minn. Stat. § 246.0141 (Supp. 2003), prohibiting the possession or use of tobacco in state-operated facilities, which included the Minnesota Sex Offender Program. The detainees first challenged the statute by arguing that it violated Minn. Const. art. IV, § 17. The purpose of this constitutional provision was to prevent what was called "log rolling legislation" or "omnibus bills" by which a number of different and disconnected subjects were united in one bill, and then carried through by a combination of interests. Nevertheless, as the district court concluded, the enactment of the statute was for the purpose of enhancing the health of individuals in regional treatment centers by eliminating the possession or use of tobacco products. The district court did not err in finding that no constitutional privacy rights existed to use or possess tobacco within these state-run facilities. Using a rational basis test, the appellate court concluded that the state goal of curtailing smoking was legitimate. The district court did not err in finding that Minn. Stat. § 246.0141 (Supp. 2003) was not in violation of the detainees' equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

457 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


J.M.P. v. Fletcher


A04-921


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 111



February 1, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by J.M.P. v. Fletcher, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 232 (Minn., Apr. 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County; Hon. M. Michael Monahan, Judge. District Court File No. C4-03-11176.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which upheld the sheriff's denial of his application for a permit to carry a firearm on the ground that he posed a substantial likelihood of danger to himself or the public.


OVERVIEW: At a hearing, there was evidence presented that appellant had made various threats, at least one resulting in a restraining order. While Minn. Stat. § 624.714, subd. 6(b) (Supp. 2003) allowed an applicant to submit additional information after an initial denial, appellant did not submit such information. The court held that because of appellant's failure to exhaust administrative remedies, the court declined to consider the sheriff's office's handling of the application. As to any surprise evidence at the trial court hearing, appellant could have used discovery procedures and all incidents involved his own past conduct. Also, while the trial court referred to the sheriff's decision, when viewed in context, the trial court concluded de novo that the statutory standard for denial of a permit had been met. The court noted that the existence of the restraining order was uncontroverted, it supported the trial court's decision, and the court considered the document itself. Finally, based on the level of harassment being serious enough to warrant a restraining order, appellant's violation of the order, and police testimony, the trial court's findings were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

In re Civ. Commitment of Johnson


A04-1361


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 18



January 18, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Civil Commitment of Johnson, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 196 (Minn., Mar. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County. Hon. Patricia L. Belois, Judge. District Court File No. P4-02-60508.
State v. Johnson, 2000 Minn. App. LEXIS 323 (Minn. Ct. App., Apr. 11, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual challenged a decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which ordered him committed as a sexually dangerous person (SDP) under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18c(a) (2002).


OVERVIEW: The individual had numerous complaints of sexual misconduct. The trial court committed the individual and the court affirmed on appeal. The court rejected the individual's claim that he was entitled to a jury trial in this matter. The Minnesota Constitution did not guarantee a right to a jury trial in a civil commitment proceeding at present. There was sufficient evidence presented to support the finding that the individual was an SDP. The trial court found that the individual engaged in a course of harmful sexual conduct, as defined in Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 7a (2002), with others. The trial court did not abuse its discretion when it relied on expert testimony, along with other corroborating evidence, in reaching its decision. Under Minn. Stat. § 253B.185, subd. 1 (2002), the individual did not show by clear and convincing evidence that a less restrictive alternative to commitment existed. The court rejected the individual's attack on a case law standard because the court had previously found that case law did not create a new standard in which those civilly committed under the lack-of-adequate-control standard might have sought redress.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

459 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Padgett


A03-1894


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 37



January 18, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County;, Hon. Michael J. Roith, Judge. District Court File Nos. K9-02-7100, K5-02-7739, K6-02-7975, K8-02-7976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree criminal sexual conduct and kidnapping in the Anoka County District Court, Minnesota. He appealed, asserting that the district court erred by failing to give the jury a specific unanimity instruction and in admitting highly prejudicial hearsay evidence. He also asserted there was insufficient evidence to support his kidnapping conviction and that the district court plainly erred in sentencing him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, because the State charged him with four acts of sexual penetration in two counts, the district court was required to instruct the jurors that they had to unanimously agree as to which acts formed the basis for each count. The appellate court held that since the jurors were instructed that they had to agree unanimously in count one that defendant sexually penetrated the victim, they did not have to be told that they had to be unanimous as to how that penetration occurred. Regarding count two, it was unarguable that defendant engaged in a single course of conduct involving various means of sexual penetration. Thus, the district court did not err in simply instructing that penetration meant sexual intercourse. Secondly, the appellate court held the district court properly allowed the victim to testify to statements defendant made about slapping his victims since same was probative as to the victim's fear. However, the victim's confinement was incidental to the sexual assault, requiring reversal of defendant's kidnapping conviction, and the district court's aggravated durational departure did not comply with the criminal friendly case of Blakely v. Washington.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for criminal sexual conduct was affirmed. His conviction for kidnapping was reversed. The matter was remanded for resentencing, as the district court had based its aggravated durational departure on facts that defendant did not admit or that were not found by the jury.

 

460 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Charles


A04-20


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 38



January 18, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Charles, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 174 (Minn., Mar. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. John L. Holahan, Judge. District Court File No. 03032550.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of fourth-degree and fifth-degree criminal sexual conduct. The Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) sentenced defendant to 102 months after concluding that he was a dangerous offender under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 1(d) (2002). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that counsel was ineffective because counsel conceded defendant's guilt to fifth-degree criminal sexual conduct during closing arguments without defendant's consent. The appellate court concluded that defendant had little opportunity to appreciate that a concession was made when counsel declined surrebuttal after the prosecutor stated that defendant conceded guilt, and there was no record of whether counsel obtained defendant's consent to such a trial strategy. Defendant also alleged that the jury instructions improperly shifted the burden of guilty to him. The appellate court found no error, noting that in the two instances where the trial court misstated the burden of proof, it quickly corrected the statement and thus, the misstatements did not result in confusion for the jury. Next, the appellate court concluded that, contrary to his contention, defendant waived his right to testify and that said waiver was counseled, knowing, and voluntary. Finally, the appellate court concluded that defendant's sentence was improperly based on factors that went beyond mere criminal history and that were not admitted or found by a jury.


OUTCOME: Defendant's claim of ineffective assistance was remanded to allow him to pursue the claim by petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant's sentence was reversed and the case remanded for resentencing consistent with the mandates of Blakely.

Whitten v. State


A04-793


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


690 N.W.2d 561; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 57



January 11, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. 99117387.
Whitten v. State, 2002 Minn. App. LEXIS 795 (Minn. Ct. App., July 9, 2002)



DISPOSITION: District court's denial of petition for post-conviction relief reversed, and conviction vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the denial of his petition for postconviction relief and his conviction by the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, of unlawful possession of a firearm. Defendant argued that a prior probation-discharge order informed him that all of his civil rights were restored, including the right to possess a firearm.


OVERVIEW: In 1992, defendant was convicted of a non-violent felony and sentenced to probation. The probation agreement defendant signed stated that any person who had been convicted as a felon could not lawfully own, use or possess a firearm until the conviction was expunged, set aside, pardoned or until civil rights were restored. In 1997, defendant was discharged from probation. The district court order stated that defendant was "discharged from probation and restored to all civil rights and to full citizenship with full right to vote and hold office the same as if said conviction had not taken place." Further, while there was a place on the order to restrict defendant's possession of a firearm for 10 years, that box was not checked. Defendant was arrested for unlawful possession of a firearm in 1999. The appellate court reversed the conviction and held that the State could not indicate that defendant had the right to possess firearms when all his civil rights were reinstated, tell him all his civil rights were reinstated, and then tell him that he should have known he could not possess a firearm. Thus, Minn. Const. art. I, § 7, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV prohibited his conviction.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the district court's denial of defendant's postconviction relief and vacated his conviction.

State v. King


A04-292


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


690 N.W.2d 397; 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 4; 27 A.L.R.6th 657



January 4, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Minn. v. King, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 184 (Minn., Mar. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. 03043279.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) of fifth-degree controlled substance crime. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying the motion to suppress because the information in the search warrant affidavit was stale because it was executed seven days after it was issued. The court of appeals disagreed. The criminal activity alleged in the affidavit was that defendant was selling drugs out of his apartment. The affidavit stated that the confidential reliable informant made a controlled purchase of crack cocaine from defendant and was given a phone number to contact him should he wish to make additional purchases. Citizens and the building's owner had complained of activity suggesting a history of drug sales from the apartment. An officer testified that the day the warrant was executed the confidential informant called defendant at the number with which he had been provided during the earlier controlled buy and confirmed that defendant was in his apartment and willing to sell narcotics. It was reasonable to conclude that the probable cause that existed at the time the search warrant was issued continued to exist when the warrant was executed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Pilot


A04-345


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1467



December 28, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Motion denied by State v. Pilot, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 225 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. Marilyn Brown Rosenbaum, Judge. District Court File No. 96040844.
State v. Pilot, 1998 Minn. App. LEXIS 659 (Minn. Ct. App., June 9, 1998)



DISPOSITION: District court's denial of petition for post-conviction relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, petitioner, challenged the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, denying his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was convicted in 1997 of first-degree criminal sexual conduct and attempted first-degree murder. The petitioner's convictions were affirmed in June 1999, and, in July 2000, the district court filed an amended sentencing order adding a five-year conditional-release term to his sentence. The petitioner argued that his sentence was unconstitutional in light of recent U.S. Supreme Court decisions, because the judge, rather than the jury, determined the existence of aggravating factors that resulted in the imposition of the 270-month sentence, rather than the presumptive guidelines sentence. The appellate court ruled that the petitioner's challenge to the constitutionality of his sentence based on the U.S. Supreme Court's decisions in Apprendi, Ring, and Blakely failed because his case was final when those cases were decided; thus, his sentence was not affected by the new procedural rules that those cases established. Also, the five-year conditional-release term was appropriately added to the petitioner's sentence, because, when the petitioner was convicted of first-degree criminal sexual conduct, Minnesota law mandated the imposition of a conditional-release term.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Eibensteiner


A04-792


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


690 N.W.2d 140; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1486



December 28, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Eibensteiner, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 141 (Minn., Mar. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Mower County District Court. File No. K4-03-1469.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded; motion to strike granted in part and denied in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a decision from the Mower County District Court (Minnesota), which dismissed a grand jury indictment charging defendant with violating laws prohibiting corporate campaign contributions.


OVERVIEW: After a grand jury returned an indictment for several election crimes, defendant filed a motion to dismiss. The district court dismissed the indictment after finding that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The State then sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the district court was permitted to dismiss the indictment under the conditions set forth in Minn. Stat. § 630.18(4) (2002). The district court had subject matter jurisdiction to hear the case under Minn. Stat. § 609.025 (2002) because the crimes were allegedly committed within Minnesota. Venue was proper in the county where the funds were derived under Minn. Stat. § 627.01 (2002). As such, the court rejected defendant's challenges under Minn. Stat. § 630.18(4) (2002) and Minn. R. Crim. P. 17.06, subd. 2. Further, the district court erred when it considered extrinsic evidence. The court rejected defendant's assertion that Minn. R. Crim. P. 11.03 applied since that rule only pertained to complaints. Finally, the court concluded that there was sufficient evidence to show that defendant committed violations of Minn. Stat. § 211B.15, subd. 2 (2002) and Minn. Stat. § 72A.12 (2002).


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

465 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fitzpatrick


A03-1480


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


690 N.W.2d 387; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1494



December 28, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Blue Earth County District Court. File No. K4-02-2043.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her conviction in the Blue Earth County District Court, Minnesota, for providing alcoholic beverages to a minor, arguing that county's compliance check violated both her due-process rights and Minnesota's statute prohibiting the underage purchase of alcoholic beverages.


OVERVIEW: The county used an underage, undercover agent in a compliance check to attempt to make a purchase of alcohol. The agent was advised to show his identification, if asked to do so. The agent also wore a cap that identified him as a member of the "Blue Earth County Sheriff's Office Alcohol Compliance Team." The agent asked defendant for a 12-pack of beer, and defendant sold the beer without asking for identification. Defendant alleged the use of the undercover and underage agent violated her due-process rights and claimed the county was prohibited from using underage, undercover officers in their compliance checks. The appellate court disagreed and affirmed defendant's conviction. The appellate court held that the officers did not manufacture a crime, but simply provided defendant with the opportunity to commit the crime; further the agent wore a cap identifying himself as a member of the compliance taskforce, and the checks were in response to the underage drinking problem in the county. The county was not prohibited from using underage officers in the compliance checks, as Minn. Stat. § 340A.503, subd. 2(2) (2002) prohibited the illegal sale of alcohol, not the illegal purchase.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Adell


A03-1897


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1428



December 21, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Adell, 2008 Minn. App. LEXIS 341 (Minn. Ct. App., Sept. 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County; Hon. Joanne M. Smith, Judge. District Court File No. K7-03-1659.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, for criminal sexual conduct. Citing nine aggravating factors, the court sentenced him to a double upward durational departure from the presumptive sentence under the sentencing guidelines. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the district court failed to give a specific unanimity instruction, failed to get his approval before instructing the jury on his right not to testify, improperly admitted certain pretrial statements, and improperly departed from the sentencing guidelines. The appellate court noted that where the State alleged ongoing criminal conduct circumscribed by specific dates, the district court properly instructed the jury on the requirement of a unanimous verdict without instructing that the jurors had to agree on a specific act or acts. The appellate court held that giving the jury instruction without defendant's permission was harmless because defendant could not demonstrate that it significantly affected the jury's verdict, and that he did not show how the victim's prior consistent statements were irrelevant to her credibility. However, the appellate court concluded that because defendant was not given an opportunity to have a jury trial on the departure factors, his sentence had to be reversed and the matter remanded on the issue of sentencing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed; however, his sentence was reversed and remanded.

State v. Habisch


A03-1787


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1429



December 21, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Habisch, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 95 (Minn., Feb. 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Pine County; Hon. Krista K. Martin, Judge. District Court File No. KX-01-1140.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Pine County District Court, Minnesota, of four controlled substance crimes. The district court sentenced him to the presumptive sentence of 115 months in prison based on the offense severity level and his criminal history score. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the district court improperly severed his case from that of his codefendant, erred by denying a motion to dismiss the charges against him because of prosecutorial misconduct, abused its discretion by denying his request for a downward durational departure, and that his sentence violated his right to equal protection. The appellate court noted that the district court did not err in denying defendant's motion for severance, as prejudice was evident because the record supported the potential for the use of antagonistic defenses at trial. The appellate court held that defendant had not shown that the fair administration of justice was compromised by the State's errant subpoena, and that the district court did not abuse its discretion by imposing the presumptive sentence because defendant did not show that substantial and compelling circumstances existed to justify a downward departure. The appellate court concluded that with respect to defendant's sentencing argument, issues that had no existence other than in the realm of future possibility were purely hypothetical and not justiciable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

468 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


A04-60


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


689 N.W.2d 796; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1431



December 21, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Stay granted by State v. Brown, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 118 (Minn., Mar. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. 02103476.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, for possession of a theft tool and sentenced to 36 months' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that classifying his offense as a felony violated his right to the equal protection of his laws and that his conviction was not supported by sufficient evidence and that aggravating factors affecting his sentence were not tried before a jury. The appellate court determined that a more severe penalty for possession of theft tools would reduce theft by reducing the ongoing occasion to engage in theft for those carrying the tools to accomplish it, this classification also met the requirements of equal protection under the Minnesota Constitution. There was sufficient evidence to support the conviction where the jury could reasonably conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant used a tool to execute the theft of the jacket. An upward departure under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 4, required an admission or a jury verdict on the added finding that the convictions formed a pattern of criminal conduct. Because the district court determined that defendant's prior convictions formed a pattern of criminal conduct, his sentence was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed; however, the matter was reversed and remanded for resentencing.

 

469 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Welfare of T.C.J.


A04-202


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


689 N.W.2d 787; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1403



December 14, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File Nos. JX-03-056554, 238043.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of the decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which found him guilty of third-degree assault and stayed an adult sentence.


OVERVIEW: The district court denied certification of defendant's assault charges and, following designation as an extended-juvenile-jurisdiction (EJJ) prosecution, a jury found him guilty of third-degree assault and not guilty of first-degree assault. On appeal from the third-degree assault conviction, he challenged in part the disposition that stayed an adult sentence. The court affirmed the rulings and instructions underlying the adjudication but, to comport with constitutional requirements, modified the disposition to vacate the stayed adult sentence. Because of the abundance of factual support in the record for the jury's verdict, the court rejected defendant's claim that the evidence was insufficient as a matter of law to support a verdict of guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court did find, however, that Minn. Stat. § 260B.130, subd. 4 (2002) was unconstitutional because, as written, the statute inevitably overweighed the prosecutor's discretion as an influence on the juvenile's sentence. That result, while clearly in violation of a juvenile's right to equal protection under law, appeared to have due process implications as well.


OUTCOME: The court modified the disposition to vacate the stayed adult sentence; the remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

 

470 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Beaulieu v. Fabian


A04-589


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1407



December 14, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County District Court. File No. C2-03-9278.
State v. Beaulieu, 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 774 (Minn. Ct. App., July 6, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the decision of the Anoka County District Court, Minnesota, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus without an evidentiary hearing. He contended his right against self-incrimination was implicated when he was mandated by respondent, the Minnesota Commissioner of Corrections, to complete a Sex Offender Treatment Program (SOTP) while his conviction for failure to register as a sex offender was pending on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner also determined that, if the inmate refused to complete a SOTP while his conviction for failure to register as a sex offender was pending on appeal, he would then be penalized by an extended period of incarceration of 150 days. The appellate court looked to a similar Kansas case, McKune v. Lile, where the United States Supreme Court heard a challenge to the Sexual Abuse Treatment Program (SATP) run by the Kansas Department of Corrections and considered how same affected an inmate's Fifth Amendment right. In the instant case, the appellate court held that, in light of the fact that a majority of the McKune court stated that extended incarceration constituted an unconstitutional compulsion, the inmate's allegations raised a factual dispute as to the implication of his privilege against self-incrimination by his participation in SOTP. Therefore, he was entitled to an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the district court's denial of the inmate's motion to vacate the 150-day sentence and remanded the matter for an evidentiary hearing.

 

471 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


A03-1853


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1397



December 8, 2004, Decided  
December 14, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. E. Anne McKinsey, Judge. District Court File No. 01080426.
State v. Dean, 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 686 (Minn. Ct. App., June 10, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of attempted first-degree murder. Defendant contended that the district court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence seized at the scene of the crime, abused its discretion by ruling that he could be impeached with his prior convictions, and erred by giving an unrequested instruction on his right not to testify.


OVERVIEW: Paramedics arrived on a scene where a victim was severely beaten. Believing defendant to also be injured, a paramedic pulled a wallet out his pocket and it was later discovered to be the victim's. Defendant was taken into custody and swabs of blood were retrieved from defendant's hands. The court held: (1) there was probable cause for defendant's arrest and the exigency of the circumstances justified obtaining evidence from defendant, such as the swabbings; (2) because defendant was lawfully arrested the wallet would inevitably have been discovered by the police; (3) the district court made extensive findings on each of the five factors set out in Jones, and because defendant's version of events was conveyed to the jury, defendant was not denied his right to testify by the ruling that he could be impeached with his prior convictions; and (4) the evidence against defendant was overwhelming and it could not be concluded that the adverse-inference instruction prejudiced defendant or that the error required a new trial. Because Blakely was decided while defendant's case was pending, the court remanded for consideration of defendant's sentence consistent with the holding of Blakely.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but remanded for resentencing.

State v. Houston


A04-324


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


689 N.W.2d 556; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1363



December 7, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, in part, Review denied by, in part State v. Houston, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 31 (2005)
Affirmed by State v. Houston, 702 N.W.2d 268, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 479 (Minn., Aug. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Sherburne County District Court. File No. K1-00-2332.
State v. Houston, 2002 Minn. App. LEXIS 1437 (Minn. Ct. App., Dec. 31, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Sherburne County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his motion for postconviction relief after he was convicted of attempted controlled substance crime in the first degree, methamphetamine manufacture, and one count of controlled substance crime in the fifth degree, possession. He was sentenced to 20 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted controlled substance crime in the first degree, methamphetamine manufacture, and one count of controlled substance crime in the fifth degree, possession. The trial court determined that he met the criteria of the career-offender statute, Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 4 (2002), and sentenced him to 20 years in prison. His conviction and sentence were upheld on direct appeal. The trial court denied his motion for postconviction relief. On appeal, the court held that defendant was not entitled to a jury trial during the sentencing proceedings. Further, because defendant offered no new legal authority allowing him to challenge the length of his sentence and because the other claims raised by him were procedurally barred under Knaffla, the court upheld the trial court's decision as to his conviction and sentence. Because other issues raised by defendant were either raised on direct appeal or could have been raised on direct appeal, the court found that they were procedurally barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

473 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hollermann


A03-930


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1372



December 7, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Hollermann, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 145 (Minn., Mar. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Isanti County; Hon. James T. Reuter, Judge. District Court File No. K402456.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with second-degree intentional murder of his wife under Minn. Stat. § 609.19, subd. 1(1) (2000) but was convicted in the Isanti County District Court (Minnesota) of second-degree felony murder under § 609.19, subd. 2(1) and sentenced him to 210 months imprisonment based on his wife's vulnerability and the particular cruelty by which the crime was committed. Defendant appealed his conviction and the upward sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant originally claimed his wife was injured in an auto accident but when the accident investigators confronted him with inconsistencies, he admitted that he had slammed her head against the inside of the car during an argument. Defendant challenged his conviction on the grounds that there was insufficient evidence and that second-degree felony murder was not a lesser-included offense of second-degree intentional murder. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, holding that felony murder was a lesser-included offense because both offenses required proof of the same elements except for the defendant's mental state, and proof of intent to kill necessarily proved malice. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in departing from the presumptive sentence of 150 months because the victim's vulnerability was listed as an aggravating factor under Minn. Sentencing Guidelines II.D.2.b. The court noted that testimony established the wife's arm was in a sling due to recent surgery and she was unable to defend herself. Because the victim's vulnerability was sufficient to support the departure the court did not address the "particular cruelty" factor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

474 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


A03-1800


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1337



November 30, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Smith, 2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 153 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. Francis J. Connolly, Judge. District Court File No. 03033288.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him of first-degree aggravated robbery, and sentencing him as a dangerous offender and as a career offender to the statutory maximum sentence of 240 months.


OVERVIEW: The victim of a robbery identified defendant as the man who took her money as she was leaving a convenience store. When the victim tried to get the money back, defendant hit her in the face several times, causing her to fall to the ground. Defendant argued that the district court abused its discretion by preventing him from questioning the victim about her mental-health history, and her related use of methadone and Celexa for treatment. The appellate court ruled that the district court did not abuse its discretion by limiting the cross-examination of the victim. Defendant was not denied the right to question the victim about her condition, but only precluded from asking about whether she was on methadone treatment or taking Celexa. The district court permitted defendant to question the victim about her use of Neurontin and Ambien, and whether she experienced any dizziness on the day of the incident. Defendant had the opportunity to cross-examine the victim regarding any relevant symptoms of prescription drug side-effects, and the record showed no evidence that her condition was impaired.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

State v. Truesdell


A04-816


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1350



November 30, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dakota County; Hon. Thomas William Bibus, Judge. District Court File No. K0-03-3198.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the pretrial order of the Dakota County District Court, Minnesota, dismissing one count of the complaint charging defendant with fifth-degree controlled substance crime.


OVERVIEW: An apartment employee observed a man, later identified as defendant, crouching and hiding by a dumpster. The employee notified police, and officers arrived at the scene shortly thereafter. The employee informed the officers that defendant had walked around one of the buildings and appeared to be concealing something. The officers subsequently located defendant and detained him. The officers noticed a glass light bulb in defendant's pocket. Based on his experience, the officer believed that the light bulb was a controlled substance pipe, and removed it from defendant's pocket. When confronted by the pipe, defendant admitted that he had used the light bulb to smoke methamphetamine near the dumpster. Subsequent lab results found trace amounts of methamphetamine on the light bulb. The appellate court ruled that the district court erred by dismissing the charge because the substance was just a "trace amount." Minn. Stat. § 152.025, subd. 2(1) (2002) did not specify a minimum amount of methamphetamine that must be present to support a conviction for fifth-degree controlled-substance crime.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed.

 

476 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Berry


A04-1565


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1307



November 23, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Redwood County; Hon. David W. Peterson, Judge. District Court File No. KX-04-33.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for aiding an offender under Minn. Stat. § 609.495, subd. 1 (2002) for driving three men who had been involved in a fatal shooting away from the scene. Defendant appealed, asserting the Redwood County District Court, Minnesota, erred in imposing a dispositional departure and a triple durational departure, based on its own findings, rather than those of a jury, in violation of her Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted it held in Hanf that dispositional departures that were based on broad offender characteristics were similar to the indeterminate sentencing decisions approved in Blakely, and therefore were not subject to Blakely's holding that the Sixth Amendment required a jury to make the findings supporting an increase in sentence. The district court's decision, based on defendant's lack of remorse and her failure in treatment, was the type of decision-making held in Hanf to be indeterminate in nature and therefore not subject to Blakely's holding. In the latter respect, defendant was properly sentenced to a dispositional departure based on the findings of the court rather than a jury. However, as to the triple durational departure, the trial court relied on aggravating factors such as the vulnerability of the shooting victims and whether they were treated with particular cruelty. That was conduct underlying the uncharged offense (in defendant's case) of second-degree murder for the victim who was killed. A departure for aiding an offender could not be based on conduct for said uncharged offense. Thus, imposition of the durational departure was error.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and the dispositional departure were affirmed, but the triple durational departure imposed on defendant by the trial court was reversed.

 

477 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Children of D.G.


A04-642


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1272



November 16, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. Jeanne J. Graham, Judge. District Court File Nos. J2-03-057102 & 161190.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother moved to dismiss a petition brought by appellee county to terminate her parental rights (TPR), arguing that it was unfair for the county to proceed, having delayed until the children were not adoptable. The mother also argued that there was no evidence in the petition that a TPR served the children's best interests. The Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) terminated her parental rights. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother first argued that the trial court erred in denying her motion to dismiss. The trial court denied the motion and ruled that the petition made a prima facie showing to support the statutory grounds pled and that it was unnecessary to make a prima facie showing that TPR was in the children's best interests. The court affirmed, stating that even if a best interests showing had been necessary the petition properly covered the issue by outlining the children's lengthy out-of-home placements and the mother's long history of noncompliance and unsuccessful programming. The mother also argued that the trial court erred when it accepted her limited waiver of trial rights. Although the mother was not questioned at length about her understanding of her trial rights, the five-day trial, where the parties called 10 witnesses and stipulated to almost 100 exhibits, provided an adequate forum for presentation of the mother's concern that the trial court consider long-term foster care. In addition, the trial court made detailed findings to support the conclusion that reasonable efforts had failed to correct the conditions leading to the children's out-of-home placements.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

478 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ekblad


A03-1617


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1281



November 16, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Martin County District Court; Hon. Robert D. Walker, Judge. File No. T403827.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted in the Martin County District Court (Minnesota) of failing to drive with due care, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 169.14, subd. 1 (2002). Appellant challenged the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's argument that the district court lacked subject-matter jurisdiction failed, as appellant had not presented any evidence that indicated that the constitutional prerequisites to the enactment of Minn. Stat. § 169.14, subd. 1 had not been satisfied. Appellant's argument that he was denied his right to counsel failed. Because appellant was not charged with a crime and did not face the threat of incarceration, no right to counsel attached. Additionally, appellant's claim that the prosecutor did not disclose all trial witnesses lacked merit, as the prosecutor told appellant that the State intended to call two officers as witnesses at trial and gave appellant copies of the police reports written by the officers (which contained the work address of both officers). There was no basis for concluding that the prosecutor committed misconduct by failing to disclose the witnesses' addresses. Finally, as both officers testified that appellant was driving too fast for the icy conditions of the road and was not using due care, the court, as fact-finder, could reasonably conclude that appellant was guilty of the charged offense.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was affirmed.

 

479 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. Kiffmeyer


A04-1775


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


688 N.W.2d 854; 2004 Minn. LEXIS 719



November 10, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Jurisdiction. Office of Appellate Courts.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner party representatives requested an order, under Minn. Stat. § 204B.44 (2002), directing the respondent Minnesota Secretary of State to place the names of party nominees for the Minnesota House of Representatives and the United States House of Representatives on a general election ballot.


OVERVIEW: The secretary of state had previously notified the party that its candidates would not appear on the general election ballot because none of the candidates had received the minimum number of votes required by Minn. Stat. § 204D.10, subd. 2 (Supp. 2003) in the primary election. On appeal, the party representatives argued if the primary threshold law was not repealed, its application to prevent the party candidates from appearing on the general election ballot was unconstitutional as a violation of their rights to associate for political purposes and to vote, as well as their rights to equal protection and due process. The supreme court weighed the burden the state's rule imposed on those rights against the interests the state contends justify that burden, and consider the extent to which the State's concerns make the burden necessary. The irrationality and arbitrariness of the primary threshold law were evident in several aspects of the statute's operation. In the absence of any suggested rational purpose for the law, the statute was unconstitutional under the First and Fourteenth Amendments. The secretary of state was ordered to certify the party's candidates.


OUTCOME: The supreme court granted the petition.

 

480 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Miskowiec v. City of Oak Grove


A04-82


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1236



November 9, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Miskowiec v. City of Oak Grove, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 27 (Minn., Jan. 20, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County; Hon. Ellen L. Maas, Judge. District Court File No. C3-01-5977.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed a decision of the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), which held that the owners were barred by the Statute of Frauds from asserting ownership of property and that no taking had occurred in the owners' action against defendant city for inverse condemnation after the city denied the owners a variance from local regulations that would have allowed them to build a single-family residence on their property.


OVERVIEW: After the father of one of the owners purchased the property in question, the city council adopted a temporary moratorium on construction in a 100-year floodplain and the property was subject to the moratorium. The father transferred the property to the owners, who applied for a variance. The court affirmed the decision and held that the owners had the right to bring a takings claim for their property because the previous owners had not applied for a variance and a taking would not have occurred until administrative remedies had been exhausted. The court held that the district court erred in the application of the Statute of Frauds. Further, it was clear that a takings claim could pass with the property's title. However, the court found evidence that the owners' property had actually increased in value since they purchased it. Finally, while the subsequent ordinances passed by the city made it even tougher for the owners to obtain a building variance, the city did not make the subject property unbuildable. The court concluded that the property started out unbuildable. The city's actions did not deprive the owners of all economically beneficial or productive use of their property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court.
