In re Civil Commitment of Sharp


A03-1904


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 727



June 29, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Review denied by In re Civ. Commitment of Sharp, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 602 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. Patricia L. Belois, Judge. District Court. File No. P9-93-35403.
In re Sharp, 2002 Minn. App. LEXIS 90 (Minn. Ct. App., Jan. 22, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee county filed a petition to commit appellant patient as mentally ill and to authorize the involuntary administration of neuroleptic medication. The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, granted the petition and civilly committed the patient. The patient appealed pro se.


OVERVIEW: On review, the patient contended the emergency-hold statute was unconstitutional as applied to her because the hold was signed by a nurse rather than a doctor. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the nurse was a registered nurse and certified nurse practitioner; further, the patient failed to raise the question nor presented any evidence that the nurse lacked qualifications. The patient did not articulate any legal argument why authorizing medication in emergencies violated her rights. Evidence that the patient had not eaten for two days prior to her hospitalization, failed to take her prescribed neuroleptic medications, refused to let a doctor examine her ankle, which had been in a cast for nearly eight months, threatened to commit suicide by jumping out of her apartment window, and kicked a nurse in the chest, lunged at another nurse, and acted aggressively toward other hospital staff was sufficient to find that she was mentally ill. Evidence showing that the patient's symptoms would continue without the medication was sufficient to support the trial court's findings that the statutory requirements for involuntary administration of neuroleptic medication were met.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

518 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Myrland


A03-1646


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


681 N.W.2d 415; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 714



June 22, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Myrland, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 551 (2004)
Subsequent appeal at State v. B.V.M., 2006 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1224 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Dakota County District Court. File No. K2-01-2646.
State v. Myrland, 644 N.W.2d 847, 2002 Minn. App. LEXIS 639 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Dakota County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of possession of pictorial representations of minors under Minn. Stat. § 617.247 (2002). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A computer lab teacher at the school where defendant taught found printed Internet photographs depicting adult men with exposed genitals on the lab's printer. The teacher immediately suspected defendant of having viewed and printed the images because months earlier defendant told the teacher he needed assistance in removing some "inappropriate" websites from his classroom computer. Defendant's computer was one of four computers that was online at the time the pictures were found. A subsequent search of defendant's computer's history found several web pages that focused on minor pornography. Defendant admitted to having viewed adult male pornography on the school's computers, but denied having viewed minor pornography. The appellate court held insufficient evidence existed to convict defendant. The internet access code was the same for all teachers on all of the school's computers, and that any number persons could also have had access to the computers. That defendant was one of many people who could have accessed the computers in question, did not prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he possessed the computers or the illegal images for purposes of § 617.247.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed.

 

519 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hartmann


A03-1674


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


681 N.W.2d 690; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 715



June 22, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Hartmann, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 565 (2004)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by State v. Hartmann, 700 N.W.2d 449, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 421 (Minn., July 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] McLeod County District Court. File No. T8-02-1801.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a judgment of the McLeod County District Court (Minnesota) convicting them of selling meat without a license, in violation of the Minnesota Consolidated Food Licensing Law, Minn. Stat. ch. 28A (2000), and selling custom-processed meat, in violation of the Minnesota Meat and Poultry Inspection Act, Minn. Stat. ch. 31A (2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that their failure to obtain a license and sale of custom-processed meat were exempt from prosecution. The court held that defendants' failure to obtain a license was not protected by Minn. Const. art. XIII, § 7 because they were not "peddlers" engaged in house-to-house vending, but instead made sales at a fixed location on a regular basis. The court held that Minn. Stat. § 28A.15, subds. 1-2 were not applicable because the phrase "products of a farm or garden occupied and cultivated" did not include the sale of meat, and the exclusion applied to persons not regularly engaged in the business. The court held that the exemption from inspections provided in Minn. Stat. § 31A.15, subd. 1(1) did not apply because defendants did not process their own meat and did not restrict its use to household members, nonpaying guests, and employees. The court noted that § 31A.15, subd. 1(4) specifically prohibited the sale of custom-processed meat. The court held that both Acts were constitutional because they were a reasonable exercise of the state's police powers that restricted the manner in which farmers could bring meat to market, but did not impinge on any fundamental right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment convicting defendants of selling meat without a license, in violation of the Minnesota Consolidated Food Licensing Law, and selling custom-processed meat, in violation of the Minnesota Meat and Poultry Inspection Act.

 

520 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jacobson


A03-1782


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


681 N.W.2d 398; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 669



June 15, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Jacobson, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 568 (2004)
Affirmed by, Certified question answered by State v. Jacobson, 697 N.W.2d 610, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 335 (Minn., June 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Dakota County District Court. File No. K6-02-3437.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with conspiracy to procure unlawful voting and conspiracy to commit forgery. The Dakota County District Court (Minnesota) denied defendant's motion to dismiss and later granted the State's motion to suppress evidence relevant to defendant's defense that he relied on the advice of counsel and on an official interpretation of the law. At defendant's request, the district court certified two questions to the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly solicited people to fill out, sign, and file voter-registration cards falsely listing defendant's adult men's club as the voter's place of residence. The district court certified the questions of whether the defenses of reliance on advice of counsel and on an official interpretation were available to defendant under Minnesota law and whether the defenses were available to defendant, as a matter of law, given the district court's finding that any reliance was unreasonable. The court held that good-faith reliance on the advice of counsel and/or on an official interpretation of the law was an available defense when intent was an element of the charged crime. Thus, the attorney's advice, if in good faith, was relevant on the issue of intent to conspire. Additionally, the district court erred in concluding that any reliance by defendant on his attorney's advice was unreasonable as a matter of law. The district court had to wait for the substance of defendant's attorney's advice to be disclosed before making a determination as to relevancy. The court also stated that evidence of reliance was admissible as a part of defendant's due process right to explain his conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's decision and remanded the case.

State v. Exposito


A03-90


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 619



June 8, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Infante, 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 620 (Minn. Ct. App., June 8, 2004)
Review denied by State v. Exposito, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 576 (Minn., Sept. 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Becker County District Court. File No. K8-00-1535.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Becker County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of first-degree controlled substance crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction of first-degree controlled substance crime, arguing that the district court erred by not warning him of the dangers of joint representation, by admitting evidence seized in the course of his arrest, and by failing to effectively remedy the State's failure to disclose that a witness was a confidential reliable informant. The court affirmed however, stating that he was not denied effective assistance of counsel because his defense attorney represented both him and his co-defendant, Minn. Const. art. 1, § 6. Defendant's allegations of conflict failed to provide even informed speculation that he was prejudiced. The record showed that defendant and the co-defendant did not have any antagonistic defenses or interests. In addition, the large amount of cash found on defendant at the time of his arrest, and the testimony of witnesses provided strong evidence of defendant's guilt. The information provided by the confidential reliable informant and corroborated by law enforcement officials provided probable cause to arrest defendant and a discovery violation was not prejudicial in light of remedial measure taken by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

522 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Nigatu v. State


A03-998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 640



June 8, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Olmsted County District Court. File No. K5-97-2633, 97-011864B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, petitioner, challenged the judgment of the Olmsted County District Court, Minnesota, denying his petition for postconviction relief from his conviction of third-degree assault.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner pled guilty to third-degree assault. Nearly two years later, the petitioner was charged in federal court with distributing cocaine and pled guilty. Based on the petitioner's criminal-history score, the federal court sentenced him to serve 108 months in prison. The petitioner subsequently moved to challenge the validity of his third-degree assault conviction. The petitioner argued that his plea was not voluntary, knowing, and intelligent, because he was not advised by the district court or defense counsel that his conviction could be used to enhance a subsequent sentence in federal court. The appellate court ruled that the district court properly advised the petitioner of his constitutional rights and the direct consequences of his guilty plea. Also, the plea petition and the petitioner's statements at the guilty-plea hearing clearly established that he was advised of the direct consequences of his plea. The enhancement effect of the petitioner's plea was a collateral consequence of the plea, about which defense counsel, like the district court, was not obligated to advise.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

523 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mattmiller


A03-472


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 624



June 8, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Mattmiller, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 524 (2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Mattmiller v. Minnesota, 543 U.S. 1021, 125 S. Ct. 663, 160 L. Ed. 2d 497, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7997 (2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Motion to strike denied by Mattmiller v. State, 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 634 (Minn. Ct. App., June 14, 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Mattmiller v. State, 2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1509 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Washington County Hon. Mary E. Carlson, Judge. District Court. File No. K0-02-2092.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Washington County Court (Minnesota) convicted defendant of failure to pay state income tax and state sales tax on his vehicles. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court allowed evidence of defendant's Oregon vehicle registration and travel vouchers as Spreigl evidence under Minn. R. Evid. 404(b). Evidence indicated defendant drove the vehicles in Minnesota; he was not an Oregon resident. He could not have legally driven the vehicles in Minnesota unless they were registered. From the Oregon vehicle registration forms, the jury could have inferred he licensed the vehicles in Oregon so he could obtain license plates while avoiding Minnesota tax. The Oregon vehicle registration application was relevant to establish the charged offense, and the trial court properly admitted the evidence. The military travel vouchers were also properly admitted. A necessary element of the crimes was that defendant was a resident of Minnesota. To prove he was a resident, it was necessary for the State to prove he was either domiciled in Minnesota, or domiciled outside Minnesota while maintaining a place of abode in the state and spending more than half the tax year in Minnesota. Error, if any, caused by statements the State made during closing argument on the travel vouchers was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

524 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Talbott


A03-921


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 611



June 1, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: St. Louis County; Hon. Mark A. Munger, Judge. District Court File No. K6-02-600877.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court, St. Louis County, Minnesota, convicted defendant of first-degree test refusal and first-degree DWI and sentenced him to the presumptive maximum, a 75-month executed sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the enhancement statute prevented "meaningful review," because the enhancement of the criminal DWI penalty was based on a civil procedure that did not require proof beyond a reasonable doubt. The court disagreed and held that reliance on defendant's prior license revocation to enhance the DWI charge was not a due process violation. As determined in recent case law, Minn. Stat. § 169A.53 (2002) provided for the required "meaningful judicial review," as it allowed for a separate judicial review, as well as administrative review, of a revocation. The court also found no error in the trial court's refusal to depart from the presumptive sentence. Defendant argued that, because he had a drinking problem, treatment would be more appropriate than the 75-month sentence. The court noted that there was little doubt that defendant had an alcohol problem, but he also had a long criminal history. At the sentencing hearing, 43 past convictions were noted; nine for felonies and nine for controlled substance or DWI offenses. The district court stated that it might have considered probation if defendant had demonstrated any ability to remain on probation or to remain sober.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re Welfare of D.Q.A.


A03-870


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 527



May 18, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. Karthryn L. Quaintance, Judge. District Court File Nos. J9-02-064313 & FAM-242942.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, challenged a decision from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which adjudicated him delinquent for the crime of possession of a pistol by minor, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 624.713, subd. 1(a) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Two police officers saw defendant drop an object as they drove by. When the object hit the ground, it sounded like metal. Defendant was stopped and questioned by the officers, and a search of the area uncovered a pistol. Defendant was then charged with a weapon offense. After he was adjudicated delinquent, defendant sought review. On appeal, the court determined that defendant waived his right to challenge the admissibility of the pistol, and addressing the issue would have worked an "unfair surprise" on the State since the record was not adequately developed. However, the court noted that the pistol would have been admissible under search and seizure law. The officers properly conducted an investigatory stop because they articulated a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity. Further, there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction, despite the fact that it was based on circumstantial evidence. The evidence introduced formed a complete chain that led directly to defendant's guilt. The district court was entitled to discredit defendant's testimony. However, the district court's failure to make the written findings constituted reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the disposition based on a failure to make sufficient written findings. The case was reversed with directions to make the appropriate findings. The rest of the district court's decision was affirmed.

State v. Johanneck


A03-671


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 530



May 18, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Johanneck, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 518 (Minn., Aug. 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Blue Earth County; Hon. Norbert P. Smith, Judge. District Court File No. K5021080.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Blue Earth County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of second-degree controlled substance possession under Minn. Stat. § 152.022, subd. 2(3) (2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the statutory distinction drawn between the quantity of hallucinogenic mushrooms possessed and the quantity of marijuana possessed violated equal protection guarantees of federal and state constitutions. He argued that the drugs should have been suppressed as fruits of an illegal search, and there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction. The appellate court found that there was no evidence to support the proposition that a person in possession of hallucinogenic mushrooms was similarly situated to a person in possession of marijuana. Defendant did not show Minn. Stat. § 152.022 prescribed different punishments or different degrees of punishment for the same conduct committed under the same circumstances by persons similarly situated. Defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied, as the fact that the warrant application did not describe every controlled substance the drug dog was certified to detect did not demonstrate that the officer acted intentionally or recklessly. Defendant agreed to a court trial pursuant to the procedures set out in a prior case. He forfeited any right to challenge the sufficiency of the evidence on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

527 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bergh


A03 -1577


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


679 N.W.2d 734; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 534



May 18, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Washington County District Court. File No. KX-02-4989.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Washington County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him of two counts of first-degree driving while impaired (DWI), both enhanced-penalty offenses, and one count of driving after revocation of his driver's license.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of DWI in Minnesota in 1994 and 2001, and his driver's license was revoked for both offenses. Defendant did not challenge the use of these convictions as aggravating factors, but he challenged the use of his DWI conviction and license revocation in Colorado in 1995 as aggravating factors as applied to the current charges. Concerning the right to consult with an attorney before deciding whether to submit to blood-alcohol testing, the appellate court determined that it was clear that the Colorado law regarding pre-test right to counsel was not in accord with the Minnesota Constitution, and the denial of assistance of counsel to defendant in Colorado violated the Minnesota Constitution, Minn. Const. I, § 6. Under Colorado law, a driver had no right to confer with counsel before deciding whether to consent to chemical testing, and, in Minnesota, a driver had a limited right to consult with an attorney. Because defendant's prior Colorado license revocation resulted from an uncounseled chemical test, it violated his Minnesota constitutional rights and could not be used to enhance defendant's current Minnesota offenses.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

State v. Pedersen


A03-249


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


679 N.W.2d 368; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 543



May 18, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Pedersen, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 523 (Minn., Aug. 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chisago County District Court. File No. K5-01-515.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Chisago County District Court (Minnesota) of felony controlled substance crime in the fifth degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a medical condition for which she used the marijuana. She testified that she smoked two to three marijuana cigarettes a day, and that the marijuana stopped her nausea and gave her an appetite. She testified that the marijuana also stopped her muscle spasms. Defendant argued, inter alia, that her conviction violated her rights to freedom of conscience. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant failed to provide any evidence that established a connection between the practice of her religion and the medicinal use of marijuana. Her belief in the medicinal use of marijuana was a personal, secular belief, driven more by her medical needs than any philosophical principle or religious tenet. The marijuana provided defendant with significant relief from her illness, but that therapeutic effect was not religious. Therefore, defendant's medicinal use of marijuana was not a sincerely held religious belief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

529 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. VanCleve


A03-1560


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 501



May 11, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Scott County; Hon. William E. Macklin, Judge. District Court File No. 2002-08868.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Scott County District Court, Minnesota, defendant was convicted of two counts of second-degree driving while impaired (DWI), which required the existence of an aggravating factor. As part of his omnibus motions, he had moved to dismiss the charges on the grounds that his 1994 license revocation could not be used as an aggravating factor to enhance the charges. The trial court had denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his 1994 license revocation should not have been used for enhancement purposes, because he was not given an opportunity to contest the revocation when his attorney in 1994 failed to file a timely implied consent petition. However, no Sixth Amendment right to counsel attached to implied consent proceedings. Therefore, the failure of defendant's attorney to have filed a timely implied consent petition in 1994 did not violate his constitutional right to counsel. Defendant also argued that his 1994 license revocation was an unconstitutional seizure, because two recent affidavits signed by him indicated that he was not driving the vehicle during the 1994 incident. However, there was no legal provision allowing defendant to perfect a collateral attack on his 1994 license revocation almost 10 years later by the simple expedient of showing the appellate court his own affidavits prepared in 2003 that addressed his theory of why a jury found him not guilty of DWI in 1994. Because the record did not indicate that defendant's 1994 license revocation was unconstitutional, the 1994 revocation was properly used to enhance his DWI charges in the instant case.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Sutton v. Sutton


A03-918


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 504



May 11, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Freeborn County; Hon. Bernard E. Borene, Judge. District Court File No. F1-00-395.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; motion to strike denied; motion for fees granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband appealed from the orders of the Freeborn County District Court, Minnesota, that awarded respondent wife sole legal and physical custody of the couple's two children, ordered the husband to pay $ 2,025 per month in child support, and temporary maintenance in the amount of $ 2,500 per month for the first two years followed by $ 2,000 for the next five years. The husband was also ordered to pay the wife $ 75,000 in attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the husband claimed that the financial obligations imposed by the trial court exceeded his ability to pay, that the trial judge erred in not ordering joint physical custody, and that the trial judge was biased and should have recused himself from the matter. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The appellate court noted that as the husband was an ophthalmologist who only worked three days a week, the trial court did not err in imputing income to the husband for the purposes of child support and maintenance. The appellate court also held that that the trial court did not err in refusing to order joint custody, as joint physical custody was disfavored in Minnesota. The trial court did not err in its distribution of the property as the husband failed to trace his nonmarital interest in the piano and the residence. Finally, the husband failed to prove that the judge was biased and should have been removed as the husband failed to raise the issue at the trial level, and the husband failed to show evidence of bias. Although the trial judge did tell the husband to "shut up," it was only after the husband had repeatedly interrupted during a proceeding.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment, denied the wife's motion to strike portion of the appellate record, and awarded the wife her attorney fees on appeal.

State v. McCloud


A03-1384


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 516



May 11, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. McCloud, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 408 (Minn., June 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. E. Anne McKinsey, Judge. District Court File No. 03028752.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with (1) careless operation of a watercraft; (2) violating rules of the road; (3) operating a boat without a fire extinguisher; and (4) operating a boat without a throwable personal flotation device. Defendant moved to suppress evidence discovered in the search of his boat. The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, granted the motion, and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A sheriff's deputy was performing water patrol and observed defendant's boat fail to yield to the deputy's boat, and almost cause a collision. After going by the patrol boat, defendant (who was driving) got off the boat and started heading toward the marina. He complied with the deputy's request to come back to the dock. The boat was searched, and the search revealed there was no fire extinguisher or life preservers on board. Defendant moved to suppress the search of the boat. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's grant of the motion. The appellate court noted that as defendant was only being arrested for a misdemeanor, the State could not rely on the search-incident-to-a-lawful-arrest exception to search the boat as under Minn. R. Crim. P. 6.01, subd. 1(1)(a), a search could only be initiated after an arrest for a misdemeanor if it reasonably appeared to the officer that arrest or detention was necessary to prevent bodily harm to the accused or another or further criminal conduct, or that there was a substantial likelihood that the accused will fail to respond to a citation. As there was no evidence supporting a custodial arrest, the search of the boat was unlawful.


OUTCOME: The grant of defendant's motion to suppress was affirmed.

 

532 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ali


A03-806


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


679 N.W.2d 359; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 517



May 11, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. 03023827.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of speeding.


OVERVIEW: An officer observed defendant's car traveling above the posted speed limit. He used a laser to confirm his suspicions. After defendant was convicted, he sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the district court did not take judicial notice of the general reliability of laser technology. However, judicial notice was appropriate based on the testing of the laser device and the training of the officer. Also, Minn. Stat. § 169.14, subd. 10(a), (b) (2002) did not violate the separation-of-powers doctrine because it did not conflict with the Minnesota Rules of Evidence. Further, the district court did not abuse its discretion by admitting the laser reading to establish defendant's speed because the officer was trained, and the device had been routinely tested for accuracy. A certificate of testing and accuracy was admissible under Minn. R. Evid. 803(6) because the certificate was reliable, and it was not prepared solely for litigation purposes. Finally, the officer's visual estimate of speed was alone sufficient to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court was affirmed.

State v. Portnoy


A03-1809


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 469



May 4, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dakota County; Hon. Kevin F. Mark, Judge. District Court File No. KX-03-1765.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota) with fleeing or attempting to flee a peace officer acting in the lawful discharge of duty. The court dismissed the charge because it found that the stop was illegal. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court erred by dismissing the case because the officer had reasonable suspicion to stop defendant's vehicle. The court of appeals agreed. Police responded to a domestic dispute between an intoxicated female and an intoxicated male. They arrived shortly after the 911 call. An officer sighted a vehicle on the left of the parking area, about 50 feet away from the townhouse where the call had originated. She shined her flashlight on the car and observed one occupant, and saw no other activity in the area. The car was the only occupied car in the parking area. As the officer continued toward the car, it began to move forward. The officer believed that the driver was possibly the male involved in the domestic altercation and told him to stop. The officer asked the driver where he had come from. The driver pointed in the direction of the townhouse and the officer asked him if he had been in any type of a fight there. The driver said that he had not. The officer asked the driver to step out of the car. At that point the driver drove off at a high rate of speed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

534 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Farrell v. City of Minneapolis


A03-1052


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 444



April 27, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County; Hon. David Duffy, Judge. District Court File No. AP 03-3297.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to respondent city's petition, the Rental Dwelling License Board of Appeals (Board), revoked appellant property owner's rental dwelling license. On review, the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, granted the city's motion to dismiss, concluding that because such quasi-judicial decisions could only be reviewed by writ of certiorari to the instant court, it lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner claimed the actions of the Board were not quasi-judicial, and the city ordinances violated the constitution. There were three considerations in determining whether a decision was quasi-judicial: (1) investigation into a disputed claim and weighing of evidentiary facts; (2) application of those facts to a prescribed standard; and (3) a binding decision. The appellate court found the Board held a hearing at which they considered the evidence, made findings of facts, applied those facts to a prescribed standard, and made a recommendation, which after approval, created a binding decision. Thus, Board's actions were quasi-judicial. Because a writ of certiorari from the court of appeals was the only method of judicial review, the district court correctly concluded that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction. However, in the context of a constitutional challenge to a statute or ordinance, the Minnesota Supreme Court had held that a party did not have to exhaust their administrative remedies by seeking a review by writ of certiorari. Thus, the district court erred in determining that it did not have jurisdiction to decide the property owner's declaratory judgment action.


OUTCOME: The district court's decision that the Board's actions were quasi-judicial and that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the matter was affirmed. However, the district court's decision that it did not have jurisdiction to decide the property owner's declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of the subject ordinance was reversed. The matter was remanded.

 

535 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Kruger v. Goodno


A04-51


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 422



April 23, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Kruger v. Goodno, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 244 (Minn., Apr. 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Nicollet County; Hon. Warren Litynski, Judge. District Court File No. C9-03-951.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This appeal was from an order of the Nicollet County District Court (Minnesota) denying appellant inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus challenging the effect of an executive order issued on July 10, 2003 on his civil commitment as a psychopathic personality. The inmate argued that the order prolonged his commitment in violation of current law.


OVERVIEW: When the inmate's criminal sentences expired, he began his civil commitment. On July 10, 2003, the governor issued Exec. Order No. 03-10, 28 Minn. Reg. 57 (July 21, 2003), which restricted future administrative releases of sexual offenders committed as sexually dangerous persons (SDP) or sexual psychopathic personalities (SPP). The inmate petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, contending that the effect of the executive order was to transform his indeterminate civil commitment into a lifetime punitive detention by foreclosing any possibility of release or discharge. The district court dismissed the petition, however, concluding that the inmate had not shown that he was presently being denied a request for a pass into the community, provisional discharge, or other release to which he would be entitled absent the governor's executive order. The instant court declined to review constitutional challenges to statutes when the party making the challenge could not show "direct and personal harm" resulting from the statute. Thus, the instant court declined to address the proper construction of the order or to decide whether the order was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

536 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Starway


A03-793


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 371



April 20, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Starway, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 546 (Minn., Aug. 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 03008287. Hon. Francis J. Connolly.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was initially found guilty of failing to maintain a fence and exceeding the maximum fence height in violation of the city code. A city inspector later returned to defendant's property and found that none of the necessary corrections had been completed. The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, found defendant not guilty of failing to maintain a fence, but guilty of exceeding the maximum fence height. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant raised several issues challenging the constitutionality of the city's fence ordinance, Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 535.420 (2003), and the discriminatory manner in which he was prosecuted; he also contended that his conviction violated double jeopardy. The appellate court disagreed, finding that § 535.420 clearly set forth the height restrictions for fences and was not so indefinite that defendant was forced to guess at its meaning. Further, the purposes set forth in Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 535.370 (2002), were legitimate. The fence ordinance accomplished the purposes for which it was created and was not unconstitutional. As defendant failed to fix the problems with his fence, his violations were part of a continuing offense. Consequently, his convictions did not violate the prohibition against double jeopardy. Although defendant argued that others in the same community were violating the same ordinance, he failed to show that the fact that he was prosecuted, while others were not, was based on an impermissible consideration such as race, religion, or the desire to prevent his exercise of a constitutional right.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

537 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burke


A03-1232


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


678 N.W.2d 68; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 383



April 20, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Burke, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 459 (Minn., July 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] St. Louis County District Court. File No. FX-85-001216.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother moved for an extension of child support from appellant father for their mentally and physically disabled son. The father challenged a decision by the child support magistrate in the St. Louis County District Court, Minnesota, that held that the father's child support obligation should continue indefinitely for his son.


OVERVIEW: The father and the mother had never married, but the father acknowledged he was the child's father and began paying support. The child, although over the age of 18, was unable to care for himself due to physical and mental disabilities. The magistrate granted the mother's motion as the child's physical and mental conditions classified him as being a child under Minn. Stat. § 518.54, subd. 2 (2002). The father challenged the decision on the grounds that the magistrate did not consider his other two children when increasing the duration of his support obligation, that the mother lacked standing to bring the motion as the child was over 18, and his equal protection rights were violated. The appellate court held that the magistrate erred in failing to consider the father's other two children when extending the support obligation indefinitely as under Minn. Stat. § 518.551 subd. 5f, those facts had to be considered when there was an increase in child support. The court noted that while the father's payments remained the same, the increase in duration constituted an increase in support. Thus, the order was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further consideration of that issue.


OUTCOME: Because the child support magistrate failed to consider the father's subsequent children when extending child support indefinitely, the matter was reversed and remanded for further consideration.

 

538 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Egan v. Hamline United Methodist Church


A03-675


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


679 N.W.2d 350; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 332



April 13, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Egan v. Hamline United Methodist Church, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 400 (2004)
Related proceeding at Gruetzmacher v. Acuity, 393 F. Supp. 2d 860, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 4485 (D. Minn., Mar. 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court. File No. C3-02-5763.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant church music director challenged a decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted respondent church's motion to dismiss the director's claims against the church for violations of the Minnesota Human Rights Act based on sexual orientation.


OVERVIEW: The director, who was bisexual, filed this action against the church and claimed that the church's demand that he write a church member a letter of apology concerning the director's claim that the member was homophobic and the director's subsequent discharge for refusing to write the letter violated the Act. The trial court dismissed the action and found that the church was not subject to the Act. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court first held that Minn. Stat. §§ 363A.20, subd. 2, 363A.26(2) (Supp. 2003) were not in conflict, as contended by the director. Because a music director played a religious role for purposes of the Act, the trial court did not err in concluding as a matter of law that the director was a church employee, not a secular employee pursuant to § 363A.26(2), and thus was exempt from the protection of the Act. The court concluded that the constitutional policy under the First Amendment of avoiding entanglement controlled in this case. The church's statements of policy did not specifically waive its exemption from the Act. Therefore, the trial court did not err in dismissing the director's claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

539 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


City of Elko v. Abed


A03-1050


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


677 N.W.2d 455; 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 360



April 13, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Review denied by City of Elko v. Abed, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 420 (Minn., June 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Scott County District. Court File No. C-02-23468.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, businesses, sought review of the decision of the Scott County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent, the City of Elko (city), in the city's action seeking an injunction to enforce Ordinance No. 92 against the sexually orientated businesses.


OVERVIEW: In 2001, the city adopted Ordinance No. 92, which established licensing requirements for sexually oriented businesses. The city subsequently filed an action against the businesses, who were operating an adult establishment that offered nude dancing. Both parties moved for summary judgment, and the district court granted summary judgment in favor of the city on all claims, Minn. R. Civ. P. 56.03. The appellate court affirmed, stating that the district court correctly concluded that the ordinance was constitutional because nude dancing received a lesser degree of U.S. Const. amend. I protection than adult films or books. The ordinance also met the three-prong Renton test. The grant of summary judgment with respect to the license and investigation fees was also appropriate because the businesses did not meet their burden to show that the fees were unreasonable. Summary judgment was also affirmed with respect to the distance restrictions and prohibition against gratuities because the distance restrictions were well defined, narrowly drawn, and did not burden more "speech" than was necessary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

540 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. New


A03-128


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 273



March 30, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Motion granted by State v. New, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 302 (Minn., May 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County District Court. File No. K3-02-2541. Hon. A. James Dickinson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of a controlled substance, arguing that the search-warrant application, which was based primarily on a controlled buy performed by a confidential informant, did not state probable cause, and that the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) erred in failing to require the State to disclose the identity of the informant.


OVERVIEW: A confidential informant was sent to defendant's apartment to make a controlled purchase of narcotics. Within 72 hours after the controlled purchase, an officer applied for and obtained a search warrant for the residence. Five days later, the warrant was executed. Defendant challenged his conviction for possession of a controlled substance. Defendant claimed that the search warrant lacked probable cause. The instant court disagreed, as the search warrant application established the informant's credibility, and the officer did not need to check the informant's lower body cavities to verify that the informant did not possess money or drugs prior to the controlled purchase. Defendant argued that the trial court should have required disclosure of the informant's identity, but, where an informant was not involved in any of the evidence on which the State relied to establish defendant's guilt, disclosure of his identity was not required. Finally, the search warrant was not stale, as only five days passed between its authorization and execution, which was within the 10 day window of opportunity, Minn. Stat. § 626.15(a) (2000).


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

 

541 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


C1-02-372, C6-02-1064


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


678 N.W.2d 1; 2004 Minn. LEXIS 119



March 11, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Jones, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 207 (Minn., Apr. 20, 2004)
Motion granted by State v. Jones (In re Jones), 2005 Minn. LEXIS 332 (Minn., May 25, 2005)
Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Jones, 753 N.W.2d 677, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 367 (2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Jones v. State, 2016 Minn. LEXIS 486 (Minn., Aug. 10, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Sherburne County Office of Appellate Courts.



DISPOSITION: Conviction reversed, denial of restitution affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder while committing criminal sexual conduct, second-degree intentional murder, and first-degree criminal sexual conduct. The Sherburne County District Court (Minnesota) entered a conviction against defendant on the first-degree murder count and sentenced him to life in prison. He appealed. After the conviction, the victim's sister petitioned for restitution, which was denied. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in: (1) finding that there was probable cause to support a search warrant; (2) admitting DNA evidence; (3) finding that there was insufficient foundation for the introduction of defendant's alternative perpetrator evidence; and (4) requiring defendant to wear a leg restraint during trial. (1) The facts underlying the warrant presented a close call as to whether there was a sufficient showing of probable cause. But, applying a deferential standard of review, sufficient probable cause existed. (2) Defendant's challenges were most appropriately characterized as going not to the admissibility of the evidence, but to its weight to be considered by the trier of fact. The DNA evidence was sufficiently reliable to be admitted. (3) Defendant's substantial rights were affected when the alternative perpetrator evidence was improperly excluded. His inability to address the exclusion of the evidence in the context of the correct legal standard seriously affected the fairness and integrity of his trial. Thus, under the plain error analysis, the conviction was reversed, and he was entitled to a new trial. (4) It was error to restrain defendant.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed, but the denial of restitution was affirmed.

 

542 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Peterson v. BASF Corp.


C3-02-857


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


675 N.W.2d 57; 2004 Minn. LEXIS 59



February 19, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Writ of certiorari granted, Vacated by, Remanded by BASF Corp. v. Peterson, 125 S. Ct. 1968, 161 L. Ed. 2d 845, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 3712 (U.S., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of Appeals. Office of Appellate Courts.
Peterson v. BASF Corp., 657 N.W.2d 853, 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 275 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a foreign corporation (corporation), sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals of Minnesota, which affirmed the district court's finding in favor of respondents, farmers, in a class action lawsuit alleging that the corporation's marketing manipulated the farmers into purchasing a higher-priced item.


OVERVIEW: The farmers executed a nationwide consumer fraud class action in which they asserted that the corporation's marketing misled and deceived the farmers into believing that a herbicide of the corporation's could not be used on crops such as sugar beets. The farmers claimed that the corporation's marketing manipulated them into purchasing a higher-priced herbicide, also a product of the corporation's. The corporation appealed the judgment rendered against it for violating the New Jersey Consumer Fraud Act (NJCFA), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 56:8-1-56:8-116 (2002). The Supreme Court of Minnesota held that the problem was the corporation's failure to seek State registration for the herbicide. Further, the corporation engaged in repeated, published, and planned misrepresentations about the herbicide's EPA regulation. It was those actions that the farmers alleged amounted to consumer fraud. Accordingly, the supreme court held that the farmers' claims under the NJCFA were not preempted by Federal Insecticide, Fungicide, and Rodenticide Act, 7 U.S.C.S. § 136 et seq.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

543 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Streiff


C8-02-1857


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


673 N.W.2d 831; 2004 Minn. LEXIS 40



January 29, 2004 Vs, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Streiff, 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 389 (Minn. Ct. App., Apr. 12, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Office of Appellate Courts.
State v. Streiff, 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 359 (Minn. Ct. App., Apr. 1, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with criminal vehicular operation resulting in substantial bodily harm and criminal vehicular operation leaving the scene of the crime. The trial court granted defendant's motion to plead guilty to two lesser-included gross misdemeanor offenses. The Minnesota Court of Appeals affirmed, holding that the State failed to show an abuse of the trial court's discretion. The State sought review.


OVERVIEW: When the trial court granted defendant's motion under Minn. R. Crim. P. 15.07 to plead guilty to two lesser-included gross misdemeanor offenses, it found that, although the State had sufficient evidence to proceed to trial, it would have been a manifest injustice to have defendant prosecuted for a felony. On review, defendant argued that the potential loss of her employment, coupled with the objection by the victim to the felony prosecution, amounted to manifest injustice. The State argued that the factors did not rise to the level of manifest injustice and that the trial court's acceptance of a plea to lesser charges violated the separation of powers provision of the Minnesota Constitution. The supreme court ruled that the standard of proof required to establish a "manifest injustice" under Rule 15.07 was at least as high as that required under Minn. R. Crim. P. 15.05, which necessitated a showing of abuse of prosecutorial discretion, and that the collateral consequences of prosecuting defendant on the felony charges did not constitute a manifest injustice.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

544 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Pawlenty


A04-84


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


673 N.W.2d 829; 2004 Minn. LEXIS 39



January 22, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Kiffmeyer, 673 N.W.2d 827, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 38 (Minn., Jan. 22, 2004).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The secretary of state referred a proposed petition to recall respondent governor to the chief justice of the supreme court for review to determine whether it alleged specific facts that, if proven, would have constituted grounds for recall of the officer under Minn. Const. art. VIII, § 6 and Min. Stat. § 211C.02 (2002).


OVERVIEW: The citizens' petition alleged three grounds for the recall of the governor; namely, nonfeasance in filing an oath of office while a member of the legislature prior to his election as governor; legal defects in the wording of the oath of office of governor he signed on January 6, 2003; and nonfeasance in the performance of his constitutional duty to take care that the laws be faithfully executed. The supreme court initially noted that recall from an elected official's current office was not permitted for alleged nonfeasance while previously holding a different office. The supreme court held that legal defects in the oath of office was not a basis for recall under Minn. Const. art. VIII, § 6 because a defect in the wording of the oath was neither malfeasance nor nonfeasance. The supreme court further held that the petition did not state facts indicating that the governor knew of an alleged violation of state law, that any failure to act on his part was intentional or repeated, or that any such failure was serious; therefore, the petition failed to state specific facts which, if proven, would have constituted grounds for recall.


OUTCOME: The citizens' petition was dismissed.

 

545 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


C8-02-790


SUPREME COURT OF MINNESOTA


673 N.W.2d 144; 2004 Minn. LEXIS 1



January 15, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of Appeals Office of Appellate Courts.
Johnson v. State, 654 N.W.2d 126, 2002 Minn. App. LEXIS 1328 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (Minnesota), which affirmed the postconviction court's judgment vacating defendant's guilty plea to sexual assault on the ground of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was placed on probation after he pleaded guilty to an unrelated charge of promoting prostitution by fraud. He was ordered to register as a predatory offender pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 609.3461 (1996) (recodified as Minn. Stat. § 609.117 (2002)) and to submit a DNA sample. After analysis of the sample, defendant was identified as a suspect in the sexual assault case, and a second blood sample was taken from defendant pursuant to a warrant. Defendant's attorney did not seek to suppress the sample obtained pursuant to the probation order, and defendant pleaded guilty. The postconviction court and the court of appeals concluded that the prostitution offense was not one for which the statute required a DNA sample and that the probation order constituted an illegal search. The court reversed, holding that the exclusionary rule did not apply because neither the statutory purpose of the DNA sample requirement nor the goal of preventing police misconduct would be served by suppression of DNA evidence seized pursuant to a court order later determined to be erroneous. Thus, defendant did not suffer actual prejudice from counsel's failure to seek suppression of the DNA evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals.

 

546 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Serena


A03-362


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


673 N.W.2d 182; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1525



December 30, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Serena, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 62 (Minn., Feb. 17, 2004)
Vacated by, Remanded by State v. Jesus Nmn, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 493 (Minn., Aug. 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Clay County District Court. File No. K6-02-509.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to aiding and abetting robbery. The Clay County District Court (Minnesota) imposed sentence and stayed the sentence with conditions. Later, the trial court revoked defendant's probation and executed the previously stayed sentence. The trial court denied defendant's motion for jail credit for time served under the extended jurisdiction juvenile statute, Minn. Stat. § 260B.130 (1998). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in refusing to give jail credit for time he was committed to a juvenile facility under the extended jurisdiction juvenile statute, Minn. Stat. § 260B.130 (1998). The appellate court ruled that credit was limited to time spent in jails, workhouses, and regional correctional facilities. Extended jurisdiction juvenile (EJJ) offenders were prevented by § 260B.130 from receiving credit for time served in juvenile facility custody if the trial court found that the EJJ offender violated the conditions of the stayed adult sentence and reasons existed to revoke the stay of the adult sentence. As defendant's time was confined in a juvenile facility, he was correctly denied credit. At the time of the violation, defendant had fair warning that jail credit would not be awarded if the trial court revoked his stayed adult sentence, and so, § 260B.130 did not violate prohibitions against ex post facto laws. The distinction between a juvenile certified as an adult and an EJJ offender was rationally related to the legitimate government goal of encouraging the rehabilitation of EJJ offenders, so § 260B.130 did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

547 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Kammueller v. Kammueller


A03-582


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


672 N.W.2d 594; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1502



December 23, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Kammueller, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 149 (Minn., Mar. 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court. File No. F7971442.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; motion granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to their divorce, appellant father and respondent mother agreed that the mother would have sole physical custody of the parties' children, but that the father would have average weekly parenting time of 38 percent. The parties did not apply the Hortis/Valento formula to calculate child support. In the instant action, the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, denied the father's motion to modify his obligation. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: Per a 1998 divorce decree, the parties had agreed that the father would pay monthly support of $ 338, somewhat less than that provided by the child-support guidelines. On appeal, the father contended that the trial court erred by refusing to modify his obligation, because he asserted his parenting time had increased substantially. He also argued that he never waived the application of the Hortis/Valento formula, which applied to instances of joint physical custody. Thus, the first issue was whether a child-support obligor's increase in parenting time, standing alone, was a sufficient basis for a downward deviation from child-support guidelines. The appellate court found the parties expressly agreed that there would be no Hortis/Valento application. Because the trial court adopted the parties' stipulation that mother would have "sole physical custody," it was not presumptively appropriate to set child support under the Hortis/Valento formula. The appellate court also rejected the father's argument that Minn. Stat. § 518.54, subd. 8 (2002) (providing that a sole physical custodian was not an obligor), violated the Equal-Protection Clauses of the state and federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The appellate court granted the father's motion to strike a portion of the wife's brief as to certain references appearing for the first time on appeal.

 

548 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Ernst v. State


A03-63


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1551



December 18, 2003, Decided  
December 30, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Ernst v. Hinchliff, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 119923 (D. Minn., July 27, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Scott County District Court. File No. 1997-11929. Hon. Thomas Howe.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed an order of the Scott County District Court (Minnesota), which summarily denied his request to vacate his conviction for indecent exposure.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pled guilty to felony indecent exposure and was sentenced to 18 months in prison. He was granted postconviction relief because the State failed to prove a prior conviction to enhance the charge to a felony level, and the conviction was treated as a conviction for gross misdemeanor indecent exposure. Petitioner filed a second petition, seeking relief from the continuing obligation to register as a sex offender under Minn. Stat. § 243.166. The district court denied the petition as untimely without a hearing. The court held that the district court did not abuse its discretion by summarily denying petitioner's second petition for postconviction relief. The relief sought was substantially the same as that sought in his first petition. The registration issue and complaints about counsel were not novel or new and could have been raised in the first petition. The court did not need to address the convict's arguments that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction and that the registration statute unconstitutionally violated due process because neither argument was raised in either of his postconviction petitions. Further, the claims were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

549 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harvey


C4-03-22


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1485



December 16, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Harvey, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 76 (Minn., Feb. 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 02047408. Hon. Delila F. Pierce.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree assault, second-degree assault, and possession of a firearm by a felon. Defendant appealed his convictions and alleged the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, erred in admitting his statements that were not voluntary, by admitting evidence of his four prior felony convictions for impeachment purposes, and by admitting evidence that he possessed a simulated controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot the victim, his girlfriend. Prior to shooting her, he placed the gun in her mouth, pulled the trigger, and chipped her teeth pulling the gun out of her mouth. Defendant admitted shooting her, but claimed the shooting was accidental. Defendant had four felony convictions within the past five years. During the police interview, the officer asked whether there was any reason why defendant's prints would be on the gun, and told defendant that the victim may not live. Defendant claimed that his statement that the shooting was accidental was not voluntary based on the officer's statements. The appellate court affirmed that defendant's statement was properly admitted as defendant had waived his rights, he had the ability to make a voluntary statement, the interrogation lasted less than an hour, and defendant did not confess to a crime. The appellate court also held that the admission of the prior felonies as impeachment evidence was proper under Minn. R. Evid. 609 as the existence of the convictions went to his credibility and his version of the facts. Finally, admission that defendant possessed a controlled substance was relevant to corroborate the victim's testimony.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed.

 

550 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Northwest Airlines, Inc. v. Metro. Airports Comm'n


A03-494


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


672 N.W.2d 379; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1492



December 16, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Northwest Airlines, Inc. v. Metro. Airports Comm'n, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 108 (Minn., Feb. 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court. File No. 62-C2-02-011974.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff airline appealed an order of the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, that dismissed its action which sought a declaratory judgment that Minneapolis-St. Paul, Minn., Ordinance 87, violated Minn. Stat. § 473.651 (2002) and was beyond defendant airport commission's authority under Minn. Stat. § 473.651 (2002). The commission argued exhaustion of administrative remedies under Minn. Stat. § 473.608, subd. 17(6) (2002) was required.


OVERVIEW: The airline argued that "may," as used in Minn. Stat. § 473.608, subd. 17(6), was permissive and thus exhaustion was not required. If the claim had been brought on constitutional grounds, the declaratory judgment action could have been an appropriate remedy. But, the claim was not a bona fide challenge to the validity or constitutionality of the ordinance, to which the doctrine of "futility" might relieve it of the exhaustion requirement. The airline asserted that rates were set too low for other airports, so it had to pay too much to subsidize the smaller "relief airports." The airline called the ordinance a violation of state law, and an ordinance interfering with its constitutional right to due process, but in reality its grievance came down to money. The commission was required to give the airline the rate relief it sought or tell the airline it was not going to give the relief sought. That denial of relief would mean the airline could then properly bring a direct lawsuit. The commission was advised to act reasonably and quickly.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

 

551 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carlson


CX-02-225


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1437



December 9, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 01095761. Hon. Mary Steenson DuFresne.
State v. Carlson, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 561 (Minn., Sept. 16, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, entered a pretrial order suppressing evidence and dismissing a driving while intoxicated (DWI) charge against defendant. The appellate court previously reversed the trial court's order; however, the Minnesota Supreme Court stayed the appeal pending the resolution of a similar case.


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed defendant driving a vehicle displaying WZ plates indicating prior DWI arrests. After the officer's patrol car passed defendant's vehicle, defendant looked at the officer, slowed his vehicle, changed lanes, and exited the highway. The officer then pursued defendant, stopped him, and arrested him for DWI. After staying defendant's appeal, the Minnesota Supreme Court held that Minn. Stat. § 168.0422 was unconstitutional and that special series plates could not provide the sole justification for a traffic stop. The appellate court held that an investigative stop required reasonable, articulable suspicion of criminal activity, and that a vehicle's display of WZ special-series plates could only be considered as one factor in the totality of the circumstances. The appellate court further held that although the police report stated that defendant looked at the patrol car as it passed to his right, any careful driver seeking to change lanes before exiting the freeway would have done the same; therefore, other than the special series license plate there was no reasonable, articulable suspicion of criminal activity to justify the traffic stop.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

552 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Schirber v. Blenkush


A03-270


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1442



December 9, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Wright County District Court. File No. F8-90-2241. Hon. Kim R. Johnson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wright County District Court (Minnesota) denied appellant father's motion to terminate or reduce his child support obligation and rejected his constitutional challenge to the inclusion of mentally impaired persons within the definition of child in Minn. Stat. § 518.54, subd. 2 (2002). The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that two of the parties' children were mentally handicapped and not self-supporting because they would not be able to take care of their basic living needs on an independent basis. Thus, the trial court then denied the father's motion to terminate or reduce his child support for those two children. Additionally, in denying the father's motion to reduce or terminate his child support obligation, the trial court found that the father was currently paying less than the child support guidelines amount and he had failed to show a substantial change in circumstances that made the existing child support amount unreasonable or unfair. The appellate court agreed with the trial court's findings. Finally, although Minn. Stat. § 518.54, subd. 2 (2002) provided the trial court jurisdiction, the father's child support obligation flowed not from the operation of the statute but from the operation of the parties' stipulation regarding the amount of child support. Therefore, the father's argument that Minn. Stat. § 518.54, subd. 2 (2002) was unconstitutional lacked an adequate factual or legal foundation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Dodd


C1-03-320


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1447



December 9, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Dodd, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 104 (Minn., Feb. 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 01056696. Hon. Margaret A. Daly.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) of six counts of possessing a pornographic work involving a minor in violation of Minn. Stat. § 617.247, subd. 4 (2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police executed a search warrant at defendant's residence and found pornographic materials. Defendant admitted to downloading such images involving children, but claimed that he was doing so in an investigation that he planned to submit to authorities. Defendant attempted to have the charges against him dismissed and claimed that Minn. Stat. § 617.247, subd. 4 (2000) was unconstitutional. The trial court denied the motion to dismiss, but found that the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad. The unconstitutional provision was severed and the State amended its complaint. Defendant was found guilty as charged, and the court affirmed on appeal. Defendant claimed that Minn. Stat. § 617.246, subd. 1(f)(2)(i), (ii) (2000) was unconstitutionally overbroad. Because defendant did not make this argument to the trial court, the court generally would have deemed the issue waived. Even were it not waived, the challenge failed because case law held that the statute subdivisions were not overbroad because they only criminalized possession of pornographic works involving real children. Because defendant's proposed jury instruction would have added an element to the crime, it was not warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

554 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kolla


A03-55


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


672 N.W.2d 1; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1417



December 2, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Freeborn County District Court. File No. T1-00-5287.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Minnesota Department of Natural Resources (the State) charged defendant nonresident minnow hauler with six counts of violating Minnesota state game and fish laws relating to the transport of minnows. The Freeborn County District Court, Minnesota, found defendant guilty as charged and imposed a 30-day stayed sentence, one year of probation, and a $ 950 fine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant challenged his convictions, arguing that he successfully asserted an affirmative defense created by Minn. Stat. § 97A.255, subd. 2(a) (2000) and the minnow-transport laws under which he was charged discriminating against interstate commerce. The appellate court held that the trial court did not err by concluding that defendant had no grounds upon which to assert the affirmative defense set forth in Minn. Stat. § 97A.255, subd. 2(a) (2000) as none of the minnows in defendant's possession came from waters licensed as aquatic farms as defined by the Minnesota Aquaculture Development Act, Minn. Stat. §§ 17.46-.4999 (2000). The appellate court also found that the 12-hour permit required of all persons to transport minnows through the state and the provision requiring an exporting minnow-hauler's vehicle license were constitutional. However, the appellate court also found that by imposing a differential license fee that favored resident minnow haulers and exporters over their nonresident counterparts, Minn. Stat. §§ 97A.475, subd. 28(1); 97C.501, subd. 4(a) (2000) discriminated against interstate commerce in violation of the Commerce Clause.


OUTCOME: Those portions of the statute in question which imposed a differential license fee that favored resident minnow haulers and exporters over their nonresident counterparts were severed from the statute and defendant's convictions under those subdivisions were reversed. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

In re Civil Commitment of Daniels


A03-623


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1378



November 18, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Civ. Commitment Of: Daniels, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 32 (Minn., Jan. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. P4-01-60448. Hon. Kevin Burke.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which civilly committed him for an indeterminate period after determining that he was a sexual psychopathic personality (SPP) and a sexually dangerous person (SDP).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was confined at a correctional facility and was almost 68 years old when a police officer petitioned for his civil commitment as a SPP and a SDP. Appellant was civilly committed for an indeterminate period. On appeal, the court found that appellant provided no legal support for his contention that the trial court was required to have evidence other than his pre-commitment behavior to support the finding of dangerousness. The court further found that the evidence in the record showed a likelihood of serious physical harm supporting the order. The findings reflected appellant's multiple physical acts of digital penetration and fondling of children, use of force and manipulation on victims, and the consequent embarrassment and humiliation of the victims. The commitment order was based on sufficient evidence of the likelihood of serious physical harm resulting from a release. Finally, the court found that the evidence of lack of control and the court-appointed examiners' opinions that they were unaware of a program providing the security necessary to protect the public defeated appellant's claim of a satisfactory alternative to commitment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

State v. Blooflat
