COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


671 N.W.2d 591; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1381



November 18, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Benton County District Court. File No. KX00484.



DISPOSITION: Reversed the sentence and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Benton County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of driving after cancellation and aggravated driving under the influence and sentenced him to two consecutive one-year prison terms.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving after cancellation and aggravated driving under the influence. He was sentenced to one year in prison for the aggravated driving under the influence conviction and one year in prison for driving after cancellation, to be served consecutively. On appeal, the court held that driving after cancellation was not a lesser-included offense of driving under the influence. Defendant was properly convicted of both offenses even though they arose out of the same course of conduct. However, the court found that Minn. Stat. § 609.035, subd. 2(g) (Supp. 1999) was unconstitutional because, by mandating consecutive sentences, it deprived defendants facing more than one-year incarceration of their constitutional right to a 12-person jury. Accordingly, the court upheld defendant's convictions but remanded the case for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the case for resentencing.

Archer-Kath v. Teachers Ret. Ass'n


A03-304


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1375



November 12, 2003, Decided  
November 18, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Archer-Kath v. Teachers Ret. Ass'n, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 29 (Minn., Jan. 20, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator teacher appealed, by writ of certiorari, a decision of respondent Teacher's Retirement Association (TRA) Board that she was not entitled to service credit for the period during which she was on leave with pay pursuant to a settlement agreement between the teacher and the school district.


OVERVIEW: The teacher argued that, because TRA provided an estimate of the value of her pension benefit at the time of her marriage dissolution, and because she relied on that estimate in entering into a marital termination agreement, TRA was estopped from denying the service credit she sought. The appellate court first needed to conclude that the TRA had authority to grant the service credits the teacher sought. The TRA Board affirmed the TRA Executive Director's determination that the payments received by the teacher had to be characterized as "severance" payments that were typically excluded from TRA's definition of salary and therefore ineligible for service credits. Even if the payments to the teacher did not constitute severance payments, the teacher did not show that they constituted payments for any type of leave for which Minn. Stat. § 354.05, subd. 35 authorized service credit. The TRA was without discretion to award retirement service credit. The teacher's leave was not among the types of leave listed for which service credit could be granted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

558 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Taylor


CX-03-218


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1349



November 10, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Taylor, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 21 (Minn., Jan. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Nicollet County District Court. File No. K902437. Hon. Warren Litynski.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's case was submitted on stipulated facts, the Nicollet County District Court (Minnesota) convicted him of the misdemeanor offenses of driving after suspension and obstructing legal process. On appeal defendant challenged the denial of his motions to suppress evidence and to dismiss the charges, arguing that he was subject to an unconstitutional seizure in violation of Minn. Const. art. I, § 10.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that a police officer blocked defendant's vehicle in order to ask defendant to move the car from the no parking zone next to a handicap parking space. Upon approaching the vehicle the officer smelled alcohol, and defendant gave false information before giving his true name and birthdate. Defendant was arrested on outstanding warrants, escaped, and was recaptured. Charges of giving a false name and birth date, and escape from custody were dismissed by the State but he was convicted of the remaining charges. The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motions to suppress. The court held that the officer's action in blocking defendant's car constituted a seizure under Minn. Const. art. I, § 10, because a reasonable person would not have felt free to end the encounter. However, the court held that the seizure was reasonable. The officer's sole purpose in approaching was to ask defendant to move his car. The court held that it was reasonable for the officer to ensure defendant would not suddenly drive away as the officer approached, and pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.346, subd. 3, the officer was authorized to enforce parking violations related to handicap spaces.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Garcia


A03-483


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


670 N.W.2d 297; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1271



October 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Garcia, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 797 (2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Garcia, 683 N.W.2d 294, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 424 (Minn., July 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Clay County District Court. File No. J0-99-50486.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Clay County District Court (Minnesota) gave appellant juvenile a stayed 58-month adult sentence after being designated an extended jurisdiction juvenile (EJJ). After he twice violated probation, the district court executed his adult sentence and refused to give him credit for juvenile custody time spent at a Minnesota Correctional Facility. Appellant challenged that refusal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, then 14, was involved in an armed robbery. Appellant was adjudicated delinquent, received a stayed adult sentence of 58 months, and was placed on supervised juvenile probation. Appellant returned to court on a probation violation. The district court found that appellant violated probation and ordered him to complete a juvenile corrections program. Appellant completed the program and was released to a foster home placement. Appellant absconded from his foster home and was subsequently arrested, certified as an adult, and charged with second-degree assault. The district court again found that he violated his probation and continued the matter until his pending adult charge had been resolved. The district court revoked appellant's EJJ status and executed his stayed 58-month adult sentence. The district denied him credit for time appellant served at the juvenile facility. Because the probation violation that led to appellant's time served at the juvenile facility occurred after the amendment to Minn. Stat. § 260B.130, subd. 5 (2002), the statute did not violate the ex post facto clause and the district court properly applied the statute and refused to grant him jail credit.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the district court's judgment.

State v. Schad


C1-03-270


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1265



October 15, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County District Court. File No. K6025384. Hon. Jenny Walker Jasper.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota) of dissemination of child pornography. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that Minn. Stat. § 617.247, subd. 8, violated due process by shifting the burden of proof on an element of the offense, namely the age of the person or persons depicted in a "pornographic work." The court of appeals disagreed. In Myrland, a saving construction of Minn. Stat. § 617.247, subd. 8, was adopted under which that provision placed on defendants only the burden of production, not the burden of persuasion. In addition, The stipulated record established that defendant sent by e-mail to a police officer posing as a 13-year-old girl pornographic pictures of girls who defendant himself represented to be about the same age as he understood the recipient to be. Defendant told the police at least some of the pictures were of girls under the age of 18. In contrast to that abundant evidence showing how the State could have met its burden of proof on the element of age, the stipulation included no evidence that the defense proposed to submit on the element of age. Therefore, even if defendant showed that the affirmative defense was unconstitutional, there were no ground to reverse his conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

562 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wohlsol, Inc.


A03-521


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


670 N.W.2d 292; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1276



October 14, 2003, Decided  
October 21, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Stevens County District Court. File No. T202385.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. First certified question answered in the affirmative. Second certified question answered in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Stevens County District Court (Minnesota) certified the questions of (1) whether Minn. Stat. § 340A.503, subd. 1(a)(1) (1998), as it related to whether appellant licensee "permitted" an underage person to drink alcohol on the licensed premises, required proof by the State that the licensee acted with knowledge of the alleged statutory violation and (2) whether the statute was unconstitutionally vague with respect to the term "permit."


OVERVIEW: The licensee was charged with two misdemeanor counts of permitting underage persons to drink alcoholic beverages on its licensed premises in violation of § 340A.503, subd. 1(a)(1). The licensee moved to dismiss the charges, claiming that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The licensee also objected to the district court's proposed jury instructions, which did not require the State to prove that the licensee had knowledge of the violation or specific intent. The district court denied the motion to dismiss but granted the licensee's request that the jury be instructed that the State was required to prove that the licensee acted with knowledge of the alleged violation. The district court then certified the two questions to the court. The court affirmed the district court's ruling and concluded that the meaning of the word "permit" as used in § 340A.503, subd. 1(a)(1), was clear and required an element of knowledge of the violation such that the licensee authorized, tolerated, or ratified the sale of intoxicating liquor to minors. Because the word "permit" unambiguously required an element of knowledge of the violation, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The first certified question was answered in the affirmative, and the second certified question was answered in the negative.

 

563 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kittrell


C9-01-2182


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1224



October 7, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at In re Civil Commitment Of: Kittrell, 2006 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 509 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Steele County District Court. File No. K698259. Hon. Gerald Wolf.
State v. Kittrell, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 281 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Steele County District Court, Minnesota, denying his motion to correct his sentence. On appeal, the instant court determined that the 10-year conditional release term could be reduced to 42 months and made to run concurrently with the supervised release term of the same duration. The State petitioned for review, and the matter was remanded for reconsideration by the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of second-degree assault. Defendant was found to be a patterned sex offender, and was sentenced to 126 months, of which 84 months were to be served in prison and 42 months on supervised release. The district court ordered defendant to provide a DNA sample, register as a sex offender, and pay restitution. The appellate court ruled that no conditional-release term could be imposed on defendant. Defendant was convicted only of second-degree assault, an offense for which the statute did not mandate any conditional-release term, Minn. Stat. § 609.222 (1996). No conditional-release term could have been imposed except under the patterned-sex-offender statute, Minn. Stat. § 609.1352, subd. 5 (1996). However, the statute operated in violation of Apprendi to increase the sentence beyond the ordinary statutory maximum based on a judicial finding. Because defendant was sentenced to a conditional-release term in addition to the statutory maximum sentence, and since there was no other authority for imposing the conditional-release term that did not rely on a judicial finding, defendant's 10-year conditional-release term had to be vacated.


OUTCOME: Denial of defendant's motion to correct his sentence was reversed.

State v. Bach


A03-10


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1232



October 7, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 01059562. Hon. Warren Sagstuen.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) of third-degree criminal sexual conduct. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred because the search pursuant to the Ramsey County warrant was unlawfully executed, and therefore, evidence discovered during the search pursuant to the Hennepin County warrant should have been suppressed under the fruit-of-the-poisonous-tree doctrine. The court of appeals disagreed. The fruit-of-the-poisonous-tree doctrine did not exclude evidence obtainable by an independent source. The information obtained from the internet service provider (ISP) linked defendant's screen name to defendant's real name and residence. The affidavit also set forth information about the chat-room dialogue between defendant and the victim indicating that defendant was providing sexual material to the victim and had personally met with the victim. There was also evidence of defendant's prior conviction for having sex with a 14-year-old boy. The evidence supported the trial court's conclusion that the information from the Ramsey County search warrant was not necessary to establish probable cause for the Hennepin County warrant and a sanitized application for the Hennepin County warrant provided independent probable cause for its issuance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Pella v. State


C9-03-274


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA

PRIOR HISTORY: Todd County District Court. File No. K500717.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Todd County District Court, Minnesota, denied defendant's petition for postconviction relief, after defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree controlled-substance crime. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a petition for postconviction relief, arguing that he was entitled to open the omnibus hearing and the increased sentence recommended by the State pursuant to the second plea agreement was the result of prosecutorial vindictiveness. The prosecutor's alleged statement did not present a violation that might warrant the appellate court's review despite the waiver. There was no element of punishment or retaliation so long as the accused was free to accept or reject the prosecution's offer.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

566 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Rooney v. Rooney


A03-53


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


669 N.W.2d 362; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1161



September 16, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Rooney v. Christ's Household of Faith, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 763 (Minn., Nov. 25, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Christ's Household of Faith v. Rooney, 541 U.S. 1011, 124 S. Ct. 2075, 158 L. Ed. 2d 621, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 3089 (2004)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Rooney v. Rooney, 2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 67 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court File No. F1-87-23807.
Rooney v. Rooney, 478 N.W.2d 545, 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1225 (Minn. Ct. App., 1991)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, a divorced husband and his ex-wife, were members of appellant church, which was ordered to perform income withholding to pay the husband's child support and spousal maintenance obligations. The church appealed, arguing it was not an employer under Minn. Stat. § 518.611 (1990). The order was reversed and remanded. The Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, ordered judgment for arrearages against the church. The church appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the church contended, inter alia, that the trial court did not have jurisdiction over the claim against the church for compliance with the child-support withholding statute. Contrary to the church's argument, the appellate court held that the trial court could apply § 518.6111 to the church without excessive entanglement in the church's religious affairs as the determination of whether the relationship between the church and the husband made the church subject to § 518.611 could be made by religiously neutral factors. Thus, the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction. The appellate court also found that requiring the church to comply with § 518.6111 did not infringe on the church's right to free exercise of religion. The state had a compelling interest in securing child support from the husband, and this interest extended to the church, or any other entity that could have been required to perform income withholding for the husband. Although the statute in question was amended before the remand was decided, the appellate court found that the results should have been the same under either version.


OUTCOME: Trial court' calculation of arrears and the amount of the husband's income to be withheld was reversed and remanded; otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

Carolla v. Am. Family Mut. Ins. Co.


A03-0021


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1109



September 9, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dakota County District Court. File No. C4-00-8633. Hon. Thomas Poch.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, insurer, brought an interlocutory challenge to the determination by the Dakota County District Court, Minnesota, that it had subject-matter jurisdiction over an action by respondent, insured, for coverage and other relief for diminished-value loss to her vehicle, and that mandatory injunctive relief should be granted. The insured filed a notice of review challenging the imposition of a bond.


OVERVIEW: The insured's leased vehicle was damaged in an accident. The insurer paid for repairs to the vehicle, and the insured filed a class-action suit asserting that the value of her vehicle was diminished as a result of being in an accident and that the insurer's policy covered the loss. The trial court granted the insured's motion for injunctive relief and effectively ordered the insurer to either change the language of its policy to specifically exclude diminished-value loss or notify a class of insureds that they were entitled to diminished-value loss. The trial court also ordered all money-damages claims were subject to mandatory arbitration, Minn. Stat. § 65B.525 (2002). The appellate court ruled that the trial court's exercise of subject-matter jurisdiction was proper because the insurer in earlier stages of the litigation had denied coverage, and the policy coverage for diminished value was a legal issue subject to judicial determination. Also, the appellate court found that the injunction was a permanent injunction, as it followed a determination on the merits, and that the issuance of the injunction and bond requirement should be reversed.


OUTCOME: The district court's exercise of subject-matter jurisdiction was affirmed, the mandatory injunction was reversed, the imposition of a bond was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

568 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Benniefield


C1-02-1991


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


668 N.W.2d 430; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1110



September 9, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, in part State v. Benniefield, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 728 (Minn., Nov. 25, 2003)
Affirmed by State v. Benniefield, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 202 (Minn., Apr. 22, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Olmsted County District Court. File No. K1-01-4417.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Olmsted County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted and sentenced him for third-degree controlled substance offense, Minn. Stat. § 152.023, subd. 2(4) (2002).


OVERVIEW: An officer saw a man that he recognized as defendant, called dispatch, and found that defendant had outstanding warrants. Defendant was arrested and during an initial search of defendant's person, the officer found a crack pipe defendant's pocket. At time defendant was 61 feet from the edge of an elementary school property line. Defendant was subsequently convicted for third-degree controlled substance offense and he appealed. The court affirmed the conviction, stating that the record showed that the district court found that defendant did not present any exceptional circumstances that would have warranted appointment of substitute counsel. Further, Minn. Stat. § 152.023, subd. 2(4) (2002), under which he was convicted, did not violate the equal protection guarantee of the Minnesota Constitution. Defendant chose to walk through a school zone with crack cocaine in his possession and in doing so he assumed a risk that he would be stopped and arrested. Thus, he failed to show that § 152.023, subd. 2(4) was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt. His sentence was improper because of the erroneous inclusion of two prior misdemeanors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment but remanded so that defendant could be sentenced according to a criminal history score of two, rather than three.

 

569 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCoy


C4-02-1788


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


668 N.W.2d 425; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1119



September 9, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Motion granted by State v. McCoy, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 724 (Minn., Nov. 18, 2003)
Reversed by State v. McCoy, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 382 (Minn., July 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court. File No. K4022208.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, on one count of misdemeanor domestic violence and sentenced accordingly. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the State sought to introduce a police report and medical records to show that defendant had assaulted the complainant in 1997. The State contended that evidence of the 1997 incident was admissible under Minn. Stat. § 634.20 (2002), which allowed the trial court to admit evidence of similar prior conduct between the defendant and another household member in domestic abuse cases. The trial court admitted the evidence although the State did not introduce the police report or the medical records. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred by admitting evidence of similar prior conduct without determining whether that conduct was proved by clear and convincing evidence. The appellate court held that unlike Minn. R. Evid. 404(b), Minn. Stat. § 634.20 (2002) did not specify an evidentiary standard by which the other conduct had to be proved. The appellate court further held a review of all applicable legislative history showed that the legislature did not intend to abrogate the clear and convincing evidence requirement and Minn. Stat. § 634.20 (2002) did not conflict with Minn. R. Evid. 404(b).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded for a new trial.

Pirila v. Pirila


C5-03-255


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1133



September 5, 2003, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Carlton County District Court. File No. F200997.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Carlton County District Court (Minnesota) granted the parties joint legal custody of their two children, awarded respondent mother sole physical custody of the children, and ordered appellant father to pay child support. The father moved to amend the custody findings and the district court denied the motion. The father appealed.

The child custody determination was affirmed because the district court did not abuse its discretion (1) by failing to make detailed findings regarding the factors listed in Minn. Further, the father's constitutional issues and the tender-years doctrine were not properly preserved for appellate review in that the father failed to raise the issues in the district court and the father failed to notify the attorney general of his challenge to the constitutionality of a Minnesota statute.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

 

571 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Granville v. Minneapolis Pub. Sch.


C6-03-135, C8-03-136


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


668 N.W.2d 227; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1102



September 2, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Granville v. Minneapolis Pub. Schs, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 731 (Minn., Nov. 18, 2003)
On remand at, Motion to strike denied by, Summary judgment denied by Granville v. Minneapolis Sch. Dist., 2005 Minn. Dist. LEXIS 137 (2005)
On remand at, Motion to strike denied by, Summary judgment denied by Johnson v. Minneapolis Sch. Dist., 2005 Minn. Dist. LEXIS 138 (2005)
Related proceeding at Granville v. Minneapolis Pub. Schs, 2005 Minn. LEXIS 618 (Minn., Sept. 20, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. PI02010663.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants were parents of students who were injured in a physical education class. The parents sued respondent school district to recover for the students' personal injuries. The school district moved to dismiss the suit, asserting that it was immune from tort liability under Minn. Stat. § 466.12, subd. 3a (2002). The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, granted the school district's motion. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents and students were African-Americans. Minn. Stat. § 466.12, subd. 3a (2002) provided immunity from tort liability, if the commissioner of insurance certified that a school district was unable to obtain insurance for a cost of $ 1.50 or less per pupil per year. The school district obtained the certification. However, the school district's student population was 45 percent African American and was the only one in the state to have received such certification. The parents argued that the statute created a class of African-American students, who were prevented from suing, that same constituted an Equal Protection Clause violation, and that strict scrutiny was applicable. However, § 466.12, subd. 3a prevented any person injured by the school district, regardless of race, from bringing suit, if the statutory requirements were met. Given alleged racial impact, Minnesota's stricter standard of rational basis review was appropriate. But, the appellate court held there was insufficient evidence from which the district court could determine whether the rate of $ 1.50 per student was arbitrary or permitted constitutional operation of the statute and dismissal was improper.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court that the rational basis standard was the appropriate level of review as to the parents' claims was affirmed. However, the judgment of the trial court dismissing the action was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings on whether the operation of the statute violated the Minnesota Constitution.

 

572 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Allina Health Sys.


C1-03-124, C0-03-213


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


668 N.W.2d 17; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1071



August 26, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Murphy v. Allina Health Sys., 2003 Minn. LEXIS 733 (Minn., Nov. 18, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court. File No. C3017776.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; certified question answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trustee for the heirs and next-of-kin of the decedent brought a wrongful-death action premised on medical malpractice against defendants, the hospital, two doctors, and the doctors' limited liability company. The Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, denied appellants' motions for summary judgment, concluding that the action was not barred by the applicable statute of limitations. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: In an amended order, the trial court certified as important and doubtful a question as to what the proper length of time was that applied to wrongful death actions premised on allegations of medical malpractice brought after August 1, 1999. On review, appellant contended that, because the legislature did not amend the wrongful-death statute of limitations when it amended the medical-malpractice statute of limitations in 1999, the wrongful-death statute continued to refer to the two-year limitations provision set forth in Minn. Stat. § 541.07 (1998). The appellate court held that the claim was governed by the statute of limitations in effect at the time the action was brought. The statute of limitations for wrongful-death actions premised on allegations of medical malpractice brought between August 1, 1999, and July 31, 2002, was four years from the date the cause of action accrued. Under Minn. Stat. § 573.02, subd. 1 (2002), the statute of limitations for wrongful-death actions premised on medical malpractice brought on or after August 1, 2002, was three years from the date of death, provided the action was brought within four years from the date the cause of action accrued.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and the certified question was answered.

 

573 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Star Tribune Co. v. Univ. of Minn. Bd. of Regents


A03-124, A03-155


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


667 N.W.2d 447; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 997



August 19, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Star Tribune Co. v. Univ. of Minn. Bd. of Regents, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 653 (2003)
Affirmed by Star Tribune Co. v. Univ. of Minn. Bd. of Regents, 683 N.W.2d 274, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 422 (Minn., July 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. MC 02-019397.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; motion to strike granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant university board conducted closed meetings with candidates for the university presidency and refused respondent news organizations' requests for data on unsuccessful candidates. Respondents sued, alleging violations of the Minnesota Open Meeting Law (OML) and the Minnesota Government Data Practices Act (DPA). The board appealed the decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which ordered the board to disclose the data.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, there were three issues: (1) whether the DPA applied to the board's search for a university president; (2) whether the OML applied to the board's search for a university president; and (3) whether the Minnesota Constitution precluded the application of the OML or the DPA to the board's search for a university president. The appellate court concluded that the DPA applied to the university's procedure for selecting its president, as Minn. Stat. § 13.02, subd. 17 specifically included the university as a state agency, and the statute had no language excluding the activity of the board's search for a university president. In addition, the OML applied to the university's procedure for selecting its president, as the OML did not contain an exception for searches for a university president. Finally, the Minnesota Constitution did not preclude imposing the OML and the DPA on the university's procedure for selecting its president, as the restrictions imposed by the DPA and the OML were merely procedural: the board could choose the president at its sole discretion, but it had to do so in accord with the DPA and the OML.


OUTCOME: The order of the district court was affirmed.

 

574 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. F.P.


CX-03-333


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


667 N.W.2d 493; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1005



August 19, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Request denied by Doe v. F.P., 2003 Minn. LEXIS 680 (Minn., Oct. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. PI-01-17801.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a wife and husband, alleged the wife was subjected to a sexual relationship with a priest against her will, and they sued defendant diocese, for sexual abuse/sexual exploitation, intentional infliction of emotional distress, loss of consortium, and negligent hiring and retention. The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, granted summary judgment to the diocese on all claims. The wife and husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issues on appeal were whether the priest provided psychotherapy within the meaning of Minn. Stat. § 148A.01, subd. 6 (2002), and whether the sexual assault statutes, Minn. Stat. §§ 609.344, subd. 1(l) and 609.345 , subd. 1(l) (2002), violated the Establishment Clause, as applied to a priest-penitent relationship. The appellate court held the priest did not provide the wife professional treatment or counseling of a mental illness, within the meaning of Minn. Stat. §§ 148A.01, subd. 6, and 148A.02 (2002). The communications regarding the intimate details of their lives, which did lead to a sexual relationship, did not come within the statutory meaning of psychotherapy. Thus, summary judgment for the diocese as to the husband and wife's claim pursuant to Minn. Stat. ch. 148A was proper. Secondly, having courts determine whether the "advice, aid, or comfort" provided by a member of the clergy in private was "religious," did not violate the Establishment Clause by fostering excessive governmental entanglement with religion. Minn. Stat. §§ 609.344, subd. 1(l), and 609.345, subd. 1(l) (2002), were not facially unconstitutional as violations of the Establishment Clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

Fletcher v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety


C9-02-2242


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 954



August 12, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Carver County District Court. File No. C6021849. Hon. Gerald W. Kalina.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent commissioner of public safety issued an order revoking appellant individual's driver's license pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169A.52, subd. 3(a) (2002) after the individual refused to take an alcohol-concentration test. The individual sought judicial review of the commissioner's order. The Carver County District Court (Minnesota) sustained the revocation of the individual's driver's license. The individual appealed.


OVERVIEW: After receiving an anonymous 911 call that there was a tan Ford Explorer proceeding eastbound on a certain road, and that the car was swerving all over the road, an officer went to the location and observed the individual erratically move into the right lane after swerving into the left turn lane. The individual's testimony about the officer's location, the officer's ability to observe the individual's driving conduct, and traffic swerving to avoid the oncoming squad car was contradicted by the officer's testimony and the tape of the 911 call. Revocation of the individual's driver's license was affirmed because (1) the officer had reasonable, articulable suspicion to stop the individual based on the information from the 911 call and the officer's observation of the individual's erratic driving; and (2) even if the officer had based the stop solely on the anonymous call, the call alone was sufficiently reliable to form a constitutional basis for the stop in that the caller described the suspect vehicle and its location, stated that the driver was "loaded," swerving all over the road, and almost hit him, and the caller described his own vehicle.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

Minn. Automatic Merch. Council v. Smith


C0-03-65


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


667 N.W.2d 159; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 973



August 12, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Minn. Automatic Merch. Council v. Smith, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 701 (2003)
Affirmed by Minn. Automatic Merch. Council v. Salomone, 682 N.W.2d 557, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 365 (Minn., June 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court. File No. C3021129.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a trade association of vending-machine operators and an operator (operators), sought a declaratory judgment that the application of the Minnesota sales tax to all sales of food in vending machines violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. art. XIV, § 1 and the Uniformity Clause of Minn. Const. art. X, § 1. The Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, granted summary judgment to respondent State. The operators appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the operators contended the classification under Minn. Stat. § 297A.61 (Supp. 2001) was unconstitutional, as it made the sale of vending-machine food always taxable, and it made the sale of the same food by others taxable only when sold in defined contexts. The appellate court first noted that Minnesota previously upheld this distinction. Applying the Miller Brewing test for determining whether there was a rational basis for the classification, the appellate court held that the limited reach of the distinction was not manifestly arbitrary and therefore, the first prong of the test was satisfied. The second prong was satisfied, as adopting a simple rule and raising revenue with administrative ease were relevant purposes of the statute. Finally, the third prong was satisfied, as the purposes and advantages of the uniform act were legitimate, and because there were legitimate reasons for not drawing distinctions between various vending-machine sales. As such, the trial court properly granted summary judgment in the State's favor.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Yeazizw


CX-02-1486


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 915



August 5, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Yeazizw, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 691 (2003)
Appeal after remand at State v. Yeazizw, 2005 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 615 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 01014419. Hon. Mary Steenson DuFresne.
State v. Yeazizw (In re Yeazizw), 2002 Minn. LEXIS 334 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of disorderly conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.72, subd. 1(3) (2000), and of obstructing legal process in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.50, subd. 1(1) (2000). She was sentenced to serve 180 days in the workhouse, with 175 days stayed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised several issues on review, including constitutional challenges to Minn. Stat. §§ 609.72, subd. 1(3), 609.50, subd. 1(1) (2000). The appellate court found that established precedent held that neither statute was unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The disorderly conduct statute's proscription of abusive and boisterous conduct applied to both defendant's speech and her physical conduct in resisting the officers and her oral statements; the obstruction of legal process statute applied to the allegations against defendant that her physical conduct interfered with the officers. Evidence of defendant's intentional physical and verbal conduct was sufficient to support her convictions. Denial of defendant's motion to dismiss for discriminatory enforcement was proper as her allegations were frivolous and conclusory. As the existence of defendant's civil lawsuit against the officers was not probative of any of the facts in the criminal case, excluding the evidence of the civil lawsuit was proper. However, the trial court's denial of a Schwartz hearing was an abuse of discretion as defendant met her evidentiary burden that jurors committed misconduct.


OUTCOME: The denial of a Schwartz hearing was reversed and remanded for further proceedings. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

In re Civ. Commitment of Chamberlain


C6-03-281


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 930



August 5, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Chamberlain, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 664 (2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Chamberlain v. Zwecker, 540 U.S. 1225, 124 S. Ct. 1520, 158 L. Ed. 2d 164, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 1746 (2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Chamberlain v. State, 2010 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 756 (Minn. Ct. App., Aug. 3, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. PX0260061. Hon. Leslie M. Metzen.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: As appellant inmate's release date approached, the department of corrections recommended that respondent State seek civil commitment of the inmate as a sexual psychopathic personality (SPP) or sexually dangerous person (SDP). After a psychological examination was conducted, the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, concluded that the inmate was an SPP and an SDP and granted the petition for commitment. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the inmate contended that the State did not prove by clear and convincing evidence that: he was an SPP; he was an SDP; or commitment to the Minnesota Sex Offender Program (MSOP) was the least-restrictive alternative. The appellate court found the inmate's convictions for attempted rape, indecent liberties, burglary with intent to commit indecent liberties, possession of child pornography, and four counts of criminal sexual conduct was sufficient evidence showing the inmate engaged in a habitual course of sexual misconduct and had an utter lack of power to control his sexual impulses. His extensive history of committing violent sexual assaults, along with doctors' testimony that it was highly probable the inmate would re-offend if not committed was sufficient evidence that the inmate was dangerous to other persons. As such, the trial court did not err by committing the inmate as an SPP and an SPD. As the inmate cited to no evidence showing that supervised release would achieve his treatment needs and the requirements of public safety, the appellate court declined to conclude that supervised release would have been an appropriate less-restrictive alternative.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Kipp v. Sweno


CX-03-140


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 936



August 5, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Kipp v. Sweno, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 703 (2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by Kipp v. Sweno, 683 N.W.2d 259, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 364 (Minn., June 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Washington County District Court. File No. C4992682. Hon. Thomas Armstrong.
Kipp v. Sweno, 629 N.W.2d 468, 2001 Minn. App. LEXIS 665 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner challenged a decision of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota), which confirmed the sheriff's execution of his homestead, ordered him not to commit waste, and awarded respondent judgment creditors attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The creditors had previously obtained a judgment against the homeowner. The trial court issued a writ of execution on the judgment, which was declared a lien against the homeowner's property. The sheriff sold the property to the creditors. The trial court confirmed the sale, awarded attorney fees to the creditors, and ordered the homeowner not to commit waste. The court affirmed in part on appeal. The homeowner's property was subject to execution as long as his wife's interest was protected. The court rejected the homeowner's claim that Minn. Stat. § 550.175, subd. 4 (2002) was unconstitutional as applied. No erroneous deprivation occurred, given that the homeowner's wife had notice of the proceedings and was given a chance to be heard. Section 550.175, subd. 4 did not violate equal protection or treat similarly situated persons differently. Because the statutory language of § 550.175, subd. 4 was clear, the court refused to find that a cash sale was required or that the credit sale to the creditors was invalid. The defect in the notice did not affect the validity of the sale. Remand was necessary on the fees issue for further fact-finding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the confirmation of the sheriff's execution and the order not to commit waste. The court reversed and remanded on the issue of attorney fees.

O'Meara v. State


C0-02-1982


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 892



July 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by O'Meara v. State, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 652 (2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by O'Meara v. State, 679 N.W.2d 334, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 264 (Minn., May 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Becker County District Court. File Nos. K899765 and KX99766. Hon. Thomas P. Schroeder.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of 2 counts of second-degree criminal sexual conduct in the Becker County District Court, Minnesota. The trial court concluded that petitioner was a patterned sex offender and sentenced him to 2 consecutive 40-year prison terms with a conditional-release period of 10 years upon completion of the prison sentence. Petitioner's petition for postconviction relief was denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court found that petitioner was a danger to public safety, as: (1) he had two prior felony convictions for criminal sexual conduct; (2) he committed the acts with the two child victims in the instant case shortly after he was released on parole for the prior convictions; and (3) he violated a position of trust in committing the acts perpetrated upon the child victims. The district court also found that, based on a psychologist's report, petitioner was in need of long-term treatment, beyond the presumptive term of imprisonment and supervised release. Citing Teague v. Lane regarding new constitutional rules of criminal procedure, the appellate court declined to apply Apprendi v. New Jersey retroactively to the petition for postconviction relief. Petitioner failed to show there was insufficient evidence to support the district court's finding that he was a patterned sex offender. Petitioner also failed to show that the facts in his case were so similar to those in the other patterned-sex-offender cases that he cited as to give rise to an equal-protection violation, and his sentence did not require a showing of "severe aggravating circumstances."


OUTCOME: The appellate court also held petitioner's sentence was within the limits of the patterned-sex-offender statute, which did not violate the constitutional prohibition of cruel and unusual punishment. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

581 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fingal


C4-02-1967, C3-03-254


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


666 N.W.2d 420; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 903



July 29, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Sub nomine at State v. Franke, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 671 (Minn., Oct. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. 67807.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were tried separately on stipulated facts, and the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) convicted defendants separately of possession of pictorial representations of minors in violation of Minn. Stat. § 617.247 (2000). Both defendants challenged the constitutionality of that statute in a consolidated appeal.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants were convicted on stipulated facts that the depictions in their possession were of real, identifiable children, and that each of them possessed large numbers of depictions. Both defendants' challenged the statute as being overly broad and violating due process. Both defendants' convictions were affirmed, as: (1) Minn. Stat. § 617.246, subd. 1(f)(1), (2)(i), 1(f)(2)(ii) (2000) were not overbroad, in that they referred only to depictions of minors or persons under the age of 18, and not to virtual or imaginary children; and (2) both defendants' lacked standing to raise the issue of due process, in that neither of them met the innocent downloader standard, both of them stipulated to possessing large numbers of works, and neither of the defendants claimed that they did not know that the persons depicted were minors. Further, the appellate court found that Minn. Stat. § 617.246, subd. 1(f)(1), (2)(i), (2)(ii) did not violate due process, as the subdivisions excluded innocent viewing and accidental downloading.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgments were affirmed.

 

582 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Hare v. State


C9-03-33


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


666 N.W.2d 427; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 914



July 29, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. 01013967.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Minnesota Department of Human Services (DHS) challenged a decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which reversed an order of DHS that affirmed respondent insurer's denial of coverage for gender reassignment surgery under Minn. Stat. § 256B.0625, subd. 3a (2002) for respondent insured.


OVERVIEW: The insured consulted with a gender-identity-disorder specialist and sought treatment for gender dysphoria. After the insured successfully completed drug treatment and participated in gender dysphoria therapy, she began hormone therapy. The insurer denied coverage for the requested gender reassignment surgery based on its determination that the insured had not commenced "gender reassignment services" before July 1, 1998, which was required by Minn. Stat. § 256B.0625, subd. 3a (2002). DHS affirmed, but the trial court reversed and found the statute unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed the trial court's decision, but did not reach the constitutional argument. The court held that "gender reassignment services" in the statute meant work done by a person who sought treatment to address the behavior and feelings of the biological sex different than his or her own. Thus, the court held that the plain meaning of the phrase included treatments for gender dysphoria and for chemical dependency required to begin hormone therapy. Because the insured completed these services prior to July 1, 1998, she met the statutory coverage requirements for the surgery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

583 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


C1-02-1229


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


664 N.W.2d 432; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 841



July 11, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Williams, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 624 (Minn., Sept. 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. 01081383.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted defendant for third-degree driving while impaired and fleeing a peace officer in a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: The State dismissed a charge of carrying a weapon without a valid permit, and defendant waived his right to take an appeal on an evidentiary ruling. On appeal, defendant argued that giving effect to the waiver of his right to appeal on a ground related to the trial court's admission of the magazines into evidence would violate public policy and the trial court abused its discretion by admitting the magazines. The appellate court held that defendant's waiver was valid and did not reach the merits of his appeal. The court found that defendant did not waive his right to appeal from a conviction on the charges of driving while impaired and fleeing a police officer in a motor vehicle or his right to appeal all of the district court's evidentiary rulings. Defendant instead waived the right to appeal a specific evidentiary ruling related to the count that the State dismissed. Thus, in return for the waiver, defendant received an important concession from the State: he no longer faced the weapon count, and his right to appeal from convictions on the other two counts was preserved. Equally important, defendant did not dispute that his waiver was knowing, intelligent, and voluntary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

584 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Benson


C4-02-2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 774



July 1, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Benson v. Minnesota, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 42369 (D. Minn., Mar. 15, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Douglas County District Court. File No. P493117. Hon. David R. Battey.
In re Benson, 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 1093 (Minn. Ct. App., Nov. 9, 1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, inmate, challenged the judgment of the Douglas County District Court, Minnesota, denying his petition for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was committed as a sexual psychopathic personality after serving a 43-month sentence for one count of first-degree criminal sexual conduct for a rape he committed in 1989. The present action was the inmate's fifth appeal to the appellate court. The appellate court ruled that because the inmate was attempting once again to raise challenges to his original commitment and because the standards applied to his original commitment satisfied the constitutional requirements of set out by the U.S. Supreme Court, the denial of the inmate's petition for habeas corpus relief was proper. Even if the basis for the inmate's original commitment was weak, the issue had been repeatedly raised and rejected, and the inmate was collaterally estopped from again raising a challenge to the validity of his original commitment. By determining that the evidence showed that the inmate was unable to control or had no control over his sexual impulses, the committing court and the appellate court on appeal made lack-of-control determinations required by the Supreme Court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

585 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Warren


C3-02-1488


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 786



July 1, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Warren, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 578 (Minn., Sept. 16, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 0822516. Hon. Lloyd B. Zimmerman.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) of possession of a firearm by an ineligible person. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence because, given the lighting conditions at the time, the police officer did not have reasonable suspicion that he possessed a gun. The court of appeals disagreed. When the officer initiated the foot chase, he knew of crack-cocaine trafficking, gang activity, and recently received citizen complaints of gunshots in the vicinity. The officer had observed defendant, who carried an object that appeared to be a gun, turn away as the squad car approached and make a furtive motion consistent with shoving this object into his waistband. With the assistance of a spotlight, the officer had observed, from 10 to 20 feet away, what appeared to be the handle of a gun sticking out of defendant's waistband. Based on that record, the officer had reasonable, articulable suspicion of criminal activity at the time the seizure occurred. Accordingly, the trial court did not err by denying the motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

586 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Atwater


C1-02-999


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 792



July 1, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Crow Wing County District Court. File No. K101586. Hon. John Leitner.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Crow Wing County District Court (Minnesota) of first-degree controlled-substance crime. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence because the search warrant was not supported by probable cause. The court of appeals disagreed. The evidence showed that the green trailer was used for personal activities and that the white trailer was used as a storage shed. The record did not show the distance between the two trailers. However, they were on opposite sides of the driveway, and there was no evidence of any enclosure surrounding the two trailers. The record did not show that defendant took steps to protect the white trailer from observation. To the contrary, an officer stated that the door to the white trailer was partially open, and its windows had no coverings. In addition, an informant's information was corroborated where the officer observed that the property's layout exactly matched the informant's description and that the white trailer contained numerous items associated with the methamphetamine-manufacturing process. The observations provided sufficient corroboration of the information provided by the informant to establish the informant's reliability. Therefore, the trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Capistrant


C3-03-27


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 807



July 1, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 02091716. Hon. Jack S. Nordby.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which determined that a police officer's stop of defendant was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The district accepted the officer's testimony that she saw defendant swerving in his lane and saw his wheels go onto the horizontal part of the curbing at some point. There was conflicting testimony as to whether construction in the area impacted defendant's driving. Noting that it could not sort out that conflicting testimony, the district court used the construction as the basis for its legal determination that the officer lacked probable cause to stop defendant. In reversing, the court reasoned that case law established the general rule that continuous weaving within one lane will justify a stop, and that rule compelled the conclusion that the stop was justified.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the officer had a constitutional basis for the stop and reversed the decision.

Pietsch v. Minn. Bd. of Chiropractic Exam'rs


C6-02-2117


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


662 N.W.2d 917; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 728



June 17, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Motion granted by Pietsch v. Minn. Bd. of Chiropractic Exam'rs, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 521 (2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by Pietsch v. Minn. Bd. of Chiropractic Examiners, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 432 (Minn., July 22, 2004)



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Affirmed in part, reversed in part; motion granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator chiropractor challenged respondent Minnesota Board of Chiropractic Examiners' conclusions that he engaged in unlawful fee splitting in violation of Minn. Stat. § 148.10, subd. 1(a)(16) (2002), and unprofessional conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. § 148.10, subd. 1(a)(11), (e) (2002).


OVERVIEW: The chiropractor contracted with a translating and transportation agency to obtain accident reports each morning to determine if members of a certain ethnic community had been injured. If so, the company contacted the victim and solicited them to become patients of the chiropractor. The company was paid for its services. The board held that the chiropractor's practices constituted fee splitting in violation of Minn. Stat. § 148.10, subd. 1(a)(16) (2002), and unprofessional conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. § 148.10, subd. 1(a)(11), (e). The appellate court reversed the finding that the chiropractor had engaged in fee splitting as § 148.10, subd. 1(a)(16) did not prohibit chiropractors from paying individuals to solicit accident victims, and there was no evidence that the chiropractor had engaged in fee splitting. The finding that the chiropractor had engaged in unprofessional conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. § 148.10, subd. 1(a)(11), (e) was upheld, as the board had the right to determine what constituted unprofessional conduct on a case by case basis. The appellate court struck that portion of the board's brief that was not supported by the record.


OUTCOME: The board's decision that the chiropractor engaged in fee splitting was reversed as it was not supported by substantial evidence, but the decision that the chiropractor engaged in unprofessional conduct was supported by substantial evidence and was affirmed on that basis. The chiropractor's motion to strike portions of the board's brief was granted in part.

State v. Cunningham


C5-02-1718


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


663 N.W.2d 7; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 693



June 10, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] St. Louis County District Court. File Nos. T702608356, TX02607945, TX02608979, T302608953, TX01603612, T902606530 T202605865, T402605866, T202608488, K302600075, T102602584, T802608642.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant indigent criminal defendants were assessed a $ 28 co-payment required by Minn. Stat. § 611.17(c) (2002). The St. Louis County District Court, Minnesota, ordered appellants to pay the co-payment and also required three of the criminal defendants to pay an additional $ 20 reimbursement to the public defenders office. The criminal defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The 10 indigent criminal defendants had all received representation from the public defenders office on misdemeanor charges, and were subsequently assessed a $ 28 co-payment under Minn. Stat. § 611.17(c) (2002). Three of the criminal defendants were also ordered to pay an additional $ 20 fee. The criminal defendants appealed and claimed that the assessment of the fee violated their rights to counsel and equal protection under the Minnesota and United States Constitutions. The appellate court affirmed the imposition of the $ 28 co-payment. The appellate court held that § 611.17(c) was constitutional as long as the requirement was not enforced against those who remained indigent or those for whom the requirement would work manifest hardship. The court also held that § 611.17(c) did not violate the equal protection clause as similarly situated persons were not being treated differently on the basis of economic status or race under § 611.17(c). The court did reverse however, the imposition of the additional $ 20 fee imposed on the three criminal defendants, as the criminal defendants had been ordered to pay more than what had been charged by the public defender.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the imposition of the $ 28 co-payment and the constitutionality of the statute, but reversed the trial court's order that required three appellants to pay an additional $ 20.

Austin Diversified Prods. v. City of Andover


C7-02-1798


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 651



June 3, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator company applied to respondent city for a license to sell cleaning products door-to-door within the city. The city clerk denied the license, and the company sought a public hearing. The city council conducted a public hearing and unanimously passed a motion upholding the city clerk's denial of the license. The company appealed by certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The company submitted a list of its employee's that would have been selling door-to-door, and a police check revealed that one person on the list had a felony warrant outstanding, the company sold products in the past after its license expired, and there were numerous citizen complaints about the company. The city ordinance specifically listed each of these as a valid reason for denying the license. The appellate court upheld the city's refusal to issue a license, as: (1) the company's constitutional challenge to the city ordinance was beyond the scope of review on appeal by certiorari; (2) the record of evidence that was before the city counsel was sufficient to support the denial of the license, and the reasons for the denial of the license were not unreasonable or arbitrary; (3) given that the company did not dispute the evidence, any concern about whether the company should have received more detailed and timely notice as to the specifics of the police incidents was effectively negated, as the company was not prejudiced; and (4) the ordinance did not allow unfettered discretion, in that the language of the ordinance was not overbroad or vague.


OUTCOME: The city counsel's decision was affirmed.

 

591 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Manypenny


CX-02-855


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


662 N.W.2d 183; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 674



June 3, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Manypenny, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 520 (2003)
Affirmed by State v. Manypenny, 2004 Minn. LEXIS 381 (Minn., July 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Becker County District Court. File No. K901534.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of fourth-degree assault of a tribal peace officer in the Becker County District Court, Minnesota. The assault occurred on White Earth tribal land. Defendant appealed, claiming that the tribal officer did not have the authority to effectuate a valid arrest of a tribal member on the White Earth reservation, and that the evidence was insufficient to sustain her conviction.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether the White Earth tribal officer, had the jurisdictional authority to arrest defendant within the boundaries of the White Earth reservation. Defendant maintained that the federal government had not granted Minnesota the right to enter into cooperative agreements with tribes to enforce criminal statutes on reservations. The appellate court noted that Public Law 280 of 1953, Pub. L. No. 83-280, 67 Stat. 588-89 (codified as amended at 18 U.S.C.S. § 1162(a)), provided Minnesota with jurisdiction over offenses committed by or against Indians in the areas of Indian country. Public Law 280 was later amended to allow state governments to retrocede its jurisdiction over a tribe. But in the specific case of the White Earth Reservation, the State had not done so. Most importantly, the State ad entered into a "cooperative agreements" with the White Earth Reservation, to "regulate the provision of law enforcement services," pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 626.93, subd. 4 (2002). The appellate court held the tribal officer was authorized to arrest defendant, and defendant's conviction was supported by sufficient evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court held the cooperative agreement between the tribe and the State of Minnesota was not invalid for the purposes of the criminal prosecution at issue. Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Shaw v. State


C1-02-937


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 675



June 3, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Shaw v. State, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 544 (Minn., Aug. 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court File No. 99126037. Robert H. Schumacher, Judge. Hon. Myron S. Greenberg.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) of aiding and abetting first-degree criminal sexual conduct. The court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence found because it was the product of an illegal search. The court of appeals disagreed. A police officer testified that the purpose for her search was to insure that there were no other people in the house after defendant and two others had been taken into custody. When the officer and her partner responded to the call, the victim was at a neighbor's house and she gave her version of the events to the officers. The victim told them she knew of at least three people in the house. She also told them a gun had been used in the incident as well as some black handcuffs and that she believed the gun would be found in defendant's bedroom in the dresser. Because the victim said that the gun would be found in a dresser in defendant's bedroom, the officer proceeded to that room. Upon entering she noticed that some of the dresser drawers were open, that she could see into the drawers, and that she saw the handcuffs. Because they were found in plain sight during a legitimate search for people and weapons at the time of the arrests, the court properly denied the motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Civ. Commitment of Martin


C3-02-2236, CX-03-168


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


661 N.W.2d 632; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 602



May 20, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Civil Commitment of Martin, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 494 (2003)
Appeal after remand at In re Civ. Commitment of Martin, 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 169 (Minn. Ct. App., Feb. 15, 2005)
Related proceeding at Martin v. Mooney, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 32912 (D. Minn., May 3, 2007)
Related proceeding at Martin v. Benson, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 73771 (D. Minn., June 14, 2010)
Post-conviction proceeding at Martin v. Benson, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 116114 (D. Minn., Sept. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Anoka County District Court. File No. PX019959.
State v. Martin, 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 75 (Minn. Ct. App., Jan. 5, 1993)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged a decision from the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), which denied its petition to have respondent patient committed under the Minnesota Sexually Dangerous Person Act (SDPA).


OVERVIEW: The patient had a long history of attempting to assault a certain victim. He pled guilty to various crimes, and he was committed to a treatment program in prison. However, he failed to complete the program and continued his assaultive behavior. Because of the patient's continued behavior, the county filed a petition to have him committed as a sexually dangerous person under the SDPA. After the county's petition was denied, it sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the district court erred when it determined that the patient's conduct toward the victim after his release from prison was not motivated by sexual impulses. Further, the patient's actions toward the victim created a substantial likelihood of serious emotional harm within the scope of Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 7a(b) (2002). In addition, a review of the patient's records indicated that he was unable to control his sexual impulses. Therefore, the district court should have determined whether or not the patient was likely to engage in future harmful sexual acts. Finally, the court found that the patient's constitutional challenges to the SDPA were meritless.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's decision to deny the county's petition. The case was remanded to the district court for a determination of whether it was highly likely that the patient would have engaged in future harmful sexual conduct.

State v. Grillo


C5-02-858


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


661 N.W.2d 641; 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 603



May 20, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Grillo, 2003 Minn. LEXIS 504 (Minn., Aug. 5, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court. File No. K8002692.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him under Minn. Stat. § 624.713, subd. 1(b) (2000), which prohibited firearm possession by individuals previously convicted of, or adjudicated delinquent for a crime of violence.


OVERVIEW: While performing an inventory search of defendant's vehicle, the officer discovered a .40-caliber automatic pistol in the passenger compartment. Defendant was previously adjudicated delinquent for felony theft of a motor vehicle, an offense that was not then characterized as a crime of violence. Because the predicated offense rendering defendant ineligible to possess a firearm was not classified as a crime of violence until after defendant had been adjudicated, defendant argued that retroactive classification of the predicated offense as a violent crime, and his subsequent prosecution and conviction for unlawful possession of a firearm, was an unconstitutional ex post facto application of the law. The appellate court ruled that neither of the challenged statutes, standing alone or in combination, violated the ex-post-facto-law prohibition, either facially or as applied to defendant. The application of Minn. Stat. § 624.712, subd. 5 (2000) to include defendant's past offense as a crime of violence merely exposed defendant to possible punishment for a future violation of possession of a firearm, Minn. Stat. § 624.713, subd. 1(b).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Holmes


C2-02-770


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 611



May 20, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 01069760. Hon. Delila F. Pierce.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of being an ineligible person in possession of a firearm. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence supporting his conviction was obtained in violation of the Minnesota and United States Constitutions after he was seized without a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity. The appellate court found that because the Minnesota Supreme Court did not adopt the United States Supreme Court's more restrictive definition of when a person had been seized, if defendant was not seized under the Minnesota Constitution, he was not seized under the United States Constitution. The officers did not seize defendant when they pulled over to talk to him. Because the officer saw the shape of a handgun in defendant's bag and defendant admitted that he had a gun, the officer had a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity and was justified in seizing defendant and the bag. Defendant's earlier conviction of being a prohibited person in possession of a firearm was one of the offenses listed in Minn. Stat. § 609.11, subd. 9 (2000), so defendant was subject to a mandatory minimum sentence of 60 months. Although Minn. Stat. § 609.11, subd. 8(b), dictated the minimum sentence that the court had to impose, it did not violate the separation-of-powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator individual appealed a decision by respondent Minnesota Metropolitan Council HRA, that denied his application for federally subsidized housing assistance.
